The Eid Khutbah: A Sunnah of Teaching and Takbir
Describes the khutbah after Eid prayer and its content about sadaqat al-fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of the Eid khutbah and explain its primary purpose of teaching the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr.

Core Idea
The Eid khutbah is sunnah muakkadah, legislated to teach the community essential rulings like sadaqat al-fitr.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the Eid khutbah's structure and purpose. The imam delivers two short sermons after the Eid prayer, following the Prophet's practice. The text emphasizes that the khutbah was legislated for teaching, particularly the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr. It also provides guidance on the use of takbir and the sitting between the two khutbahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the khutbah after Eid prayer. The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended), not fard or wajib.
The text states 'then the imam delivers two khutbahs after the prayer, following the action of the Prophet.' This shows it is based on his practice.
2
Recognize the structure
Two khutbahs delivered after the prayer, with a light sitting between them. The imam begins with takbir (not tahmid) in Eid khutbahs.
In Jumu'ah, the imam begins with tahmid; in Eid, with takbir.
3
Understand the purpose
The primary purpose is teaching (ta'lim), especially rulings of sadaqat al-fitr. The text explicitly says 'the khutbah was legislated for that i.e., for teaching.'
The teaching should cover: upon whom it is obligatory, to whom, from what, the amount, and the time of obligation.
4
Note the recommended takbir
Takbir is part of the khutbah but should not dominate. The recommended number is nine in the first khutbah and seven in the second, based on practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.
There is no fixed number in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), but the khatib should say more takbir in Adha than in Fitr.
5
Apply the ruling
The imam should focus on teaching rather than lengthy takbir. The congregation listens attentively and silently recites takbir and salawat.
The khutbah is valid even without teaching, but its legislative purpose is not fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يخطب الإمام بعد الصلاة خطبتين) اقتداء بفعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ( يعلم فيهما أحكام صدقة الفطر) لأن الخطبة شرعت لأجله قوله : (بعد الصلاة) هذا بيان الأفضلية قوله : (يعلم فيهما أحكام صدقة الفطر) أي في إحداهما وهي الأولى، وهذا في خطبة الفطر، وسيأتي بيان الأضحية، وكذا كل حكم احتيج إليه قوله لأن الخطبة شرعت لأجله أي لأجل التعليم. قال صاحب البحر بحثاً : وينبغي للخطيب أن يعلمهم الأحكام في جمعة قبل العيد لأن المندوب في صدقة الفطر فيذكر من تجب عليه ولمن تجب ومم تجب ومقدار الواجب ووقت الوجوب، ويجلس بين الخطبتين جلسة خفيفة، ويكبر في خطبة العيدين وليس لذلك عدد في ظاهر الرواية لكن لا ينبغي أن يجعل أكثر الخطبة التكبير ويكبر في خطبة عيد الأضحى أكثر مما يكبر في خطبة الفطر كذا في قاضيخان ويبدأ الخطيب بالتحميد في الجمعة وغيرها، ويبدأ بالتكبير معه بن في خطبة العيدين ويستحب أن يستفتح الأولى بتسع تترى والثانية : قال عبد الله بسبع مسعود: هو السنة ويكبر القوم ويصلون على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في أنفسهم امتثالاً للأمر وسنة الإنصات
Then the imam delivers two khutbahs after the prayer, following the action of the Prophet, teaching in them the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr, because the khutbah was legislated for that purpose. His statement: (after the prayer) this is an explanation of preference. His statement: (teaching in them the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr) meaning in one of them, the first, and this is in the khutbah of Fitr, and the explanation of udhiyah will come, and likewise every ruling needed. His statement: because the khutbah was legislated for that, i.e., for teaching. The author of al-Bahr said by investigation: It is befitting for the khatib to teach them the rulings in the Jumu'ah before the Eid because the recommended in sadaqat al-fitr... so he mentions upon whom it is obligatory, for whom it is given, from what it is given, the amount of the wajib, and the time of obligation. And he sits between the two khutbahs a light sitting. And he says takbir in the khutbah of the two Eids, and there is no set number in the apparent narration, but it should not make the majority of the khutbah takbir. And he says more takbir in the khutbah of Adha than in Fitr, thus in Qadikhan. And the khatib begins with tahmid in Jumu'ah and other than it, and begins with takbir in the khutbah of the two Eids. And it is mustahabb to open the first with nine consecutive takbirs and the second with seven, as Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: it is the sunnah. And the people say takbir and send blessings on the Prophet silently, obeying the command, and the sunnah of listening attentively.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage discusses the khutbah (sermon) of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha. The imam delivers two khutbahs after the Eid prayer, following the sunnah of the Prophet. The purpose of the khutbah is to teach the rulings related to the occasion, such as sadaqat al-fitr. The commentator explains that the teaching should cover: who must give, to whom, from what type of food, the amount, and the time of obligation. The khutbah includes sitting between the two parts, and takbir is pronounced without a fixed number, but it is recommended to have nine takbirs in the first khutbah and seven in the second. The congregation should recite takbir and salutations silently. The khutbah should not be dominated by takbir; the focus is on teaching.

Key Terms
خطبة العيدين (khutbat al-'idayn): The two sermons delivered by the imam after the Eid prayer, containing teachings and takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of the khutbah in Eid prayer according to this passage?
A) To recite takbir continuously
B) To teach the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr and other needed matters
C) To praise the imam
D) To make du'a for the community

Key Takeaway
The Eid khutbah is a sunnah muakkadah that primarily serves to teach the community the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr and other necessary matters.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Definition and Foundational Rulings of Zakat
Definition and obligation of zakat with proof and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of zakat, identify its conditions and pillars, and explain the ruling of immediate obligation.

Core Idea
Zakat is a fard obligation; delaying it without excuse is sinful and leads to punishment.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi establishes the foundational rulings of zakat: its definition, the conditions of obligation, and the immediate nature of its payment. We also learn who is exempt (prophets) and the severe consequences for neglect. The Quranic verse provides the primary proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the opening definition: zakat is a transfer of ownership of specific wealth to specific recipients. The commentator states it is obligatory (fard) upon specific persons. Identify the hukm level.
The text says 'fardat' (made obligatory) – fard, not just wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The verse from Surah At-Tawbah (9:103) is quoted: 'Take from their wealth a charity...'. In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'khudh' indicates obligation.
The dalil is Quranic, mutawatir in transmission (qati al-thubut) but zanni al-dalala in the exact ruling of fard.
3
Analyze the conditions
The text lists: free, Muslim, legally responsible (mukallaf), owner of nisab. Also, one must possess the nisab for a full lunar year (asbab).
Conditions are shurut for obligation; possession for a year is the sabab.
4
Note the immediate obligation
The commentator states it is wajib immediately (ala al-fawr) and that fatwa is upon this. Delaying without excuse incurs sin and rejection of testimony.
This contrasts with views allowing delay for valid reason.
5
Understand the exemptions
Prophets are not obligated because they have no personal ownership; their wealth is a trust. Also, they are sinless and thus not in need of purification through zakat.
This is a nuanced exception based on prophetic status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة هي تمليك مال مخصوص لشخص مخصوص فرضت على حر مسلم مكلف مالك فرضت في السنة الثانية من الهجرة كالصوم قبل فرضه وهي واجبة على الفور، وعليه الفتوى فيأثم بتأخيرها بلا عذر وترد شهادته، والأنبياء لا تجب عليهم الزكاة لأنهم لا ملك لهم مع الله إنما كانوا يشهدون أن ما في أيديهم ودائع يبذلونه في أوان بذله، ويمنعونه عن غير محله، ولأن الزكاة إنما هي طهرة لمن عساه أن يتدنس والأنبياء مبرؤن من الدنس لعصمتهم ذكره السيد، وهي طهرة لصاحبها من الذنوب قال الله تعالى: {خذ من أموالهم صدقة تطهرهم وتزكيهم بها} [التوبة : ۱۰۳] ولها معانٍ أخر، وهي البركة يقال : زكت النفقة إذا بورك فيها، والمدح يقال : زكى نفسه إذا مدحها والثناء الجميل يقال : زكي الشاهد إذا أثنى عليه، وتسمى صدقة لدلالتها على صدق العبد في العبودية منح، ورأى ليلة أسري به قوماً يسرحون كالإبل على أقبالهم رقاع، وعلى أدبارهم رقاع يسرحون كما تسرح الإبل يأكلون الضريع، وهو الشجر ذو الشوك والزقوم قيل : إنه لا يوجد في الدنيا، وقيل: شجر يوجد بتهامة نتن الريح، ورضف جهنم أي حجارتها المحماة والحجارة فسأل جبريل عنهم، فقال: هؤلاء الذين لا يؤدون زكاة أموالهم وقال الأجهوري: قيل : ورد أن على مانع الزكاة سبعين لعنة، وعلى اليهود واحدة وعلى النصارى واحدة وفي معراج القليوبي ورد في الحديث الحسن «أنه ينزل من السماء كل يوم وليلة اثنتان وسبعون لعنة منها إحدى وسبعون على مانع الزكاة وواحدة على اليهود، ورواية عكس هذا خطأ، وإذا مات صاحب المال الذي لا يؤدي زكاته استمرت الملائكة تكتب عليه هذه اللعنات إلى يوم القيامة وإن وقع في يد من يزكيه وإنما جوزوا بهذا الطعام، وهذا الملبس لأنهم منعوا المال وصرفوه في المطاعم الطيبة لتحسين بواطنهم، والملابس الطيبة لتحسين ظواهرهم، فجوزوا بضد ما فعلوا نقله بعض المشايخ. قوله : (هي
Book of Zakat. It is the transfer of ownership of specific wealth to a specific person, made obligatory upon a free, Muslim, legally responsible, property-owning person. It was made obligatory in the second year after Hijrah, like fasting before its obligation. It is obligatory immediately, and upon this is the fatwa; thus one sins by delaying it without excuse, and his testimony is rejected. Prophets are not obligated to pay zakat because they have no ownership alongside God; rather they bear witness that what is in their hands is a trust, they give it when it is time to give, and withhold it from other than its proper place. Also, zakat is a purification for one who might become defiled, while prophets are free from defilement due to their sinlessness, as mentioned by al-Sayyid. It is a purification for its owner from sins. Allah said: 'Take from their wealth a charity to purify them and cleans them thereby' [At-Tawbah: 103]. It has other meanings: blessing - one says 'zakat al-nafaqa' when it is blessed; praise - one says 'zakka nafsahu' when he praises it; and beautiful commendation - one says 'zakki al-shahid' when he lauds him. It is called sadaqah because it indicates the truthfulness of the servant in servitude. He saw on the night of the Ascension people grazing like camels, with rags on their chests and rags on their backs, grazing as camels graze, eating al-dari' (thorny shrub) and al-zaqqum. It is said that it does not exist in the world, and it is said that it is a tree found in Tihamah, foul-smelling. And radf of Hell, meaning its heated stones. He asked Jibril about them, and he said: These are those who do not pay zakat on their wealth. Al-Ujhuri said: It is reported that there are seventy curses on the one who withholds zakat, one curse on the Jews, and one on the Christians. In the ascent of al-Qalyubi, it is reported in a good hadith: 'Every day and night, seventy-two curses descend from heaven; seventy-one of them are for the one who withholds zakat, and one for the Jews.' The opposite narration is an error. If the owner of wealth who does not pay zakat dies, the angels continue to write these curses upon him until the Day of Judgment, even if the wealth falls into the hands of one who will pay zakat. They are punished with this food and clothing because they withheld wealth and spent it on good foods to improve their insides, and nice clothes to improve their outsides, so they are punished with the opposite of what they did, as narrated by some scholars. He said: ('hiya')
Source pages p. 713

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the definition and basic rulings of zakat from the commentary of Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah. It begins with the matn defining zakat as the transfer of ownership of specific wealth to a specific person. The commentator then adds that zakat is obligatory (fard) upon a free, Muslim, legally responsible, property-owning person. It was made obligatory in the second year after the Hijrah, like fasting. It is wajib immediately (ala al-fawr) according to the relied-upon position, so delaying without excuse is sinful and leads to rejection of testimony. Prophets are not obligated because they have no personal ownership; their wealth is a trust from God, and they are sinless and pure. The commentator then discusses the term 'zakat' having multiple meanings: purification (as in the Quranic verse), blessing, praise, and commendation. It is also called sadaqah because it proves the servant's truthfulness in worship. The commentator then narrates a hadith about the punishment for those who withhold zakat, seen by the Prophet on the Night of Ascension: people grazing like camels on thorny plants and hot stones, representing the food and clothes they enjoyed while withholding zakat. This is accompanied by a discussion of curses and the continuation of punishment even after death. The passage ends with the beginning of the next clause 'قوله : (هي', indicating the commentator will further explain the matn's next words.

Key Terms
زكاة (zakāt): A legally obligatory transfer of ownership of specific wealth to specific recipients
صدقة (ṣadaqah): Another name for zakat, indicating the servant's truthfulness in worship
تطهر (taṭhīr): Spiritual purification from sins

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the consequence of delaying zakat without a valid excuse?
A) One sins and his testimony is rejected
B) One becomes a disbeliever
C) The zakat becomes null and void
D) One must pay double the zakat

Key Takeaway
Zakat is an immediate fard obligation; deliberate delay without excuse constitutes a major sin.

Conditions for Zakat on Currency and Trade Goods
Opening statement listing conditions for zakat obligation on wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five conditions for zakat on currency and trade goods and apply them to a given scenario to determine if zakat is wajib.

Core Idea
Zakat is wajib on growing nisab-level wealth free from debt and basic needs after one full lunar year.

This passage opens the chapter on zakat by enumerating the essential conditions for zakat to become obligatory on wealth in the form of currency or trade goods. It is a concise matn statement that forms the basis of the chapter. Understanding these conditions is the first step in correctly applying zakat rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wealth types covered
The passage states that zakat applies to 'currency (nqood), even if in bullion, jewelry, or utensils, or what equals its value from trade goods.' Note that these are all forms of gold/silver or items of trade whose value equals the nisab.
Currency includes modern paper money and coins, valued in gold or silver.
2
Extract the conditions from the text
Read the Arabic carefully: 'free from debt and from one's basic needs, growing (in value) even if only potentially, and a condition for the obligation of its payment is the completion of a year over the nisab.' List each condition.
The passage mentions five conditions: nisab, free from debt, free from basic needs, growth (actual or potential), and one year.
3
Understand 'growing even if only potentially'
Growth (nama) can be actual (e.g., trade profit) or potential (e.g., gold/silver that can be sold or traded). This includes idle wealth that is capable of being used for investment.
Hanafi school includes potential growth; this is why gold and silver jewelry are zakatable even if not actively traded.
4
Note the hierarchy of conditions
Conditions are not equal: nisab and year are threshold; freedom from debt and basic needs ensures wealth is genuinely surplus; growth ensures wealth is productive.
These conditions prevent zakat from being due on necessary or non-growing assets.
5
Apply to a sample scenario
Take a scenario: a person has 200g of silver jewelry (value above nisab) used for decoration, no debts, and owned for 8 months. Check each condition to see if zakat is wajib.
Since the year has not completed, zakat is not yet wajib, but after 4 more months it will be.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة لنصاب من نقد ولو تبراً، أو حلياً، أو آنية، أو ما يساوي قيمته من عروض تجارة فارغ عن الدين وعن حاجته الأصلية نام ولو تقديراً وشرط وجوب أدائها حولان الحول على النصاب
The Book of Zakat: For a nisab of currency, even if in bullion, jewelry, or utensils, or what equals its value from trade goods, free from debt and from one's basic needs, growing (in value) even if only potentially, and a condition for the obligation of its payment is the completion of a year over the nisab.
Source pages p. 714

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on zakat by enumerating the essential conditions for zakat to become obligatory on wealth that is in the form of currency (nqood) or trade goods. The nisab must be from gold or silver (including jewelry and utensils) or from trade goods whose value equals the nisab. The wealth must be free from debts and from personal necessities (like basic clothing, housing, and tools); it must be growing, either actually (through trade or breeding) or potentially (capable of growth); and one lunar year must pass while the nisab remains intact. This is a concise matn statement that forms the basis of the chapter.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth (e.g., 85g gold or 595g silver) upon which zakat is obligatory.
حلي (huliyy): Jewelry made of gold or silver, regardless of permissibility of use.
حولان الحول (hawalan al-hawl): Completion of one lunar year during which the nisab remains in one's possession.
نام (naami): Growing, either actually (through trade or breeding) or potentially (capable of increasing in value).
حاجة أصلية (hajat asliyya): Basic needs such as housing, clothing, food, tools of trade, and means of transport.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for zakat on wealth?
A) The wealth must be in one's possession for two years
B) The nisab must be free from debt and basic needs
C) The wealth must be obtained through trade only
D) Zakat is due immediately upon acquiring the nisab

Key Takeaway
Zakat on currency and trade goods becomes wajib only when the wealth meets the conditions of nisab, freedom from debt and basic needs, growth potential, and completion of one lunar year.

Definition of Zakat as Transfer of Ownership
Commentary defining zakat's essential element as ownership transfer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish tamlik mal from ibaha and manfa'ah in the Hanafi definition of zakat, and apply this distinction to determine the validity of zakat payment.

Core Idea
Zakat requires transfer of ownership (tamlik mal); mere permission to use (ibaha) or providing a service (manfa'ah) does not fulfill the obligation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi legal definition of zakat as 'transfer of ownership' (tamlik mal). The passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the precise boundaries of what constitutes valid zakat, excluding mere permission to benefit (ibaha) and usufruct (manfa'ah). Understanding this distinction is critical for ensuring that one's zakat is legally valid in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal definition
The passage defines zakat as 'tamlik mal' (transfer of ownership). Note that this is the position of the verified scholars (muhaqqiqun) and is essential for the validity of zakat.
The definition is not merely descriptive; it has legal consequences for what counts as zakat.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil and its interpretation
The author cites Quran 22:22 ('And give the zakat from it'). The imperative 'آتوا' indicates obligation, and the word 'منه' implies giving from the wealth, which the Hanafis interpret as transfer of ownership.
The linguistic analysis distinguishes between the verbal meaning (the act of giving) and the derived noun (the form).
3
Distinguish tamlik from ibaha and manfa'ah
The passage explicitly excludes ibaha (mere permission to use) and manfa'ah (benefits/usufruct) from the definition. Only the transfer of ownership of a tangible asset ('ayn) qualifies as mal for zakat.
This distinction prevents substituting services or temporary use for actual ownership transfer.
4
Apply to practical examples
The passage gives examples: feeding an orphan requires handing over possession; clothing requires the recipient to understand taking possession; housing a poor person for a year is insufficient because it is only ibaha.
These examples illustrate the boundary between valid and invalid zakat payments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمليك مال هو ما عليه المحققون من أهل الأصول لأنها وصفت بالوجوب الذي هو من صفات الأفعال وموضوع علم الفقه فعل المكلف حموي، وإطلاقه على القدر المخرج مجاز شرعي، وقوله تعالى: (وآتوا الزكاة منه ) [ الحج : ۲۲] أو المراد إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود كما في أقيموا الصلاة وفي حاشية السيد الإيتاء أي الذي هو التمليك معنى مصدري والفرق بينه وبين الحاصل بالمصدر أن المعنى المصدري هو الإيقاع، والمعنى الحاصل بالمصدر هو الهيئة الموقعة ا هـ، وأخرج بالتمليك الإباحة، فلا تكفي فيها فلو أطعم يتيماً ناوياً به الزكاة لا تجزيه إلا إذا دفع إليه المطعوم كما لو كساه بشرط أن يعقل القبض در، والمال ما يتمول، أو يدخر للحاجة، وهو خاص بالأعيان وخرج بالمال المنفعة، فلو أسكن فقيراً داره سنة ناوياً للزكاة لا يجزيه در
The transfer of ownership of wealth (tamlik mal) is what the verified scholars among the usuliyyun are upon, because it (zakat) has been described with obligation (wujub), which is a description of actions, and the subject matter of fiqh is the action of the mukallaf (Hammawi). Its application to the specific extracted amount is a legal metaphor (majaz shar'i). His statement: 'And give the zakat from it' (Quran 22:22) – or it means bringing it forth from non-existence to existence, similar to 'establish the prayer'. In the Hashiya of al-Sayyid, it is stated that 'giving' (ita'), which is tamlik, is a masdari meaning. The difference between the masdari meaning and the derived noun (hukm al-masdar) is that the masdari meaning is the occurrence, while the derived noun is the form of occurrence. By 'tamlik', ibaha (permissibility) is excluded, so it is not sufficient. If one feeds an orphan with the intention of zakat, it does not suffice unless the food is handed over to him (into his possession), similarly if he clothes him, provided the orphan understands taking possession. Wealth (mal) is what is considered valuable (mutamawwal) or stored for need, and it is specific to physical assets ('ayan); benefits (manafi') are excluded by 'mal'. So if one houses a poor person in his house for a year intending zakat, it does not suffice.
Source pages p. 714

Commentary
This passage defines zakat legally as 'transfer of ownership' (tamlik mal), not just permission to benefit. The author explains that the scholars of usul define it this way because calling it 'wujub' (obligation) is appropriate for actions. The term 'zakat' applied to the specific amount is a legal metaphor. Quranic evidence (22:22) is cited, and the distinction between the verbal meaning (the act of giving) and the derived noun (the form) is clarified. Practical implications: feeding an orphan without transferring ownership does not count as zakat; similarly, providing housing (a benefit) is insufficient. This ruling guards against substituting services or temporary use for actual ownership transfer.

Key Terms
تمليك مال (tamlik mal): The legal act of transferring ownership of wealth from the payer to the recipient.
إباحة (ibaha): Mere permission to benefit without transfer of ownership.
مال (mal): Tangible property that can be stored and has value; excludes usufruct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between tamlik and ibaha in the context of zakat according to this passage?
A) Tamlik is permissible; ibaha is forbidden
B) Tamlik involves transfer of ownership; ibaha only gives permission to use
C) Both are equally valid for zakat
D) Ibaha is required for zakat; tamlik is not

Key Takeaway
Zakat in the Hanafi school is valid only when it involves the transfer of ownership (tamlik mal) of a tangible asset; mere permission to benefit (ibaha) or providing a usufruct (manfa'ah) does not discharge the obligation.

The Specific Amount of Zakat and the Condition of the Recipient
Commentary on the specific amount and recipient condition of zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific amount of zakat on the nisab (2.5%) and identify the condition that the recipient must be from the eligible categories (asnaf) with the requirement that the owner's benefit is completely severed.

Core Idea
Zakat is exactly 2.5% of the nisab and must be given to a recipient completely separate from the giver's benefit.

This lesson unpacks two key elements from the commentary on 'makhsus': the precise amount of zakat and the condition of the recipient. The amount is one-quarter of one-tenth (2.5%) of the nisab, which is agreed upon across schools. However, the recipient must not only be from the eight asnaf but also such that the giver has no remaining interest in the wealth, reinforcing the principle of sincere devotion to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate where the passage defines the 'specific' (makhsus) amount and the 'specific' person (recipient). The first pertains to the quantity of zakat, the second to the eligibility of the receiver.
2
Determine the exact amount
The text states 'one-quarter of a tenth of the nisab'. Calculate: 1/4 × 1/10 = 1/40 = 2.5%. This applies to gold, silver, and trade goods.
For livestock and produce, the rate may differ, but the passage mentions 'what takes its place from the charities of grazing animals'.
3
Understand the recipient condition
The recipient 'must be poor' or belong to other specified categories (asnaf). Critically, the giver's own slave master cannot receive, and the benefit must be completely cut off from the owner.
This means zakat cannot be given to someone from whom the giver derives direct benefit, such as a dependent or a creditor.
4
Connect to the broader Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi school defines eight eligible categories (asnaf) for zakat. The passage emphasizes the condition of severing benefit, which overrides mere poverty if the recipient is financially tied to the giver.
The exclusion of the slave master is a clear example: the master benefits from the slave's property, so giving zakat to the master would not cut off benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (مخصوص) وهو ربع عشر النصاب، أو ما يقوم مقامه من صدقات السوائم قوله : (الشخص مخصوص هو أن يكون فقيراً، ونحوه من بقية المصارف غيرها شمي، ولا مولاه بشرط قطع المنفعة عن المملك من كل وجه الله تعالى.
His statement: '(makhsus)' – it is one-quarter of a tenth of the nisab, or what takes its place from the charities of grazing animals. His statement: 'the person (makhsus)' – it is that he be poor, and likewise from the rest of the channels (asnaf) other than it (i.e., other than the poor? unclear), and not his slave master, with the condition that the benefit is completely cut off from the owner, for the sake of Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 714

Commentary
This commentary clarifies two key points from the original matn: first, the specific amount of zakat is one-quarter of a tenth (i.e., 2.5%) of the nisab, or equivalent from grains and livestock. Second, the recipient (the 'person' makhsus) must be poor, or belong to other eligible categories (the eight asnaf), with the exception that the giver's own slave master cannot receive zakat. There is a condition that the benefit must be entirely cut off from the owner, meaning the giver should have no remaining interest in the wealth given as zakat.

Key Terms
ربع عشر النصاب (rub' ushr al-nisab): One quarter of one tenth of the nisab, i.e., 2.5% of the nisab.
مصارف (masarif): The categories of recipients eligible to receive zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) One-quarter of a tenth
C) One tenth
D) One-fifth of a tenth

Key Takeaway
The specific amount of zakat on the nisab is 2.5% and the recipient must be from the eligible eight asnaf with the condition that the giver's benefit is completely severed.

Conditions for Zakat Obligation: Free, Muslim, Mature
Commentary on conditions of zakat payer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for zakat obligation in the Hanafi school and apply the rulings on apostates and the insane.

Core Idea
Zakat is obligatory only upon a free, Muslim, adult of sound mind.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the basic qualifications required for zakat to be wajib. Understanding these conditions prevents common errors when determining who must pay. The text also addresses special cases like apostates and the insane, showing careful legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
From the passage, list the three conditions explicitly: freedom (حر), Islam (مسلم), and legal maturity (مكلف). These are prerequisites for zakat obligation.
Each condition excludes a category: slave, disbeliever, minor/insane.
2
Understand the exclusions
Note that each condition excludes a specific group: slaves are excluded by 'free', disbelievers (including apostates) by 'Muslim', and minors/insane by 'mukallaf'.
The exclusion of apostates is based on the principle that an apostate is not addressed with the branches of Shari'ah during apostasy.
3
Analyze the apostate case
The text says an apostate is not obligated for acts of worship during apostasy. If he returns to Islam, he does not make up missed obligations from that period. Also, if apostasy occurs after zakat became wajib, it lapses.
This contrasts with schools that hold apostates accountable for missed acts.
4
Examine the insane person
If a person is insane the entire year, no zakat is due. If sanity returns during the year, the correct Hanafi view (Imam Abu Hanifa) requires sanity at both the beginning and end of the lunar year for obligation.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; the mufta bihi is the Imam's position.
5
Apply the conditions
In practice, zakat is not due on wealth owned by minors, insane persons, slaves, or non-Muslims. Use these conditions as a checklist when determining zakat obligation.
Remember that for the insane, the condition of mukallaf is nuanced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (على حر) خرج العبد ونحوه . قوله : (مسلم) خرج الكافر، ولو مرتداً بناء على أنه غير مخاطب بفروع الشريعة فلو أسلم المرتد لا يخاطب بشيء من العبادات أيام ردته، ولو ارتد بعد وجوبها سقطت بحر قوله : (مكلف) أي بالغ عاقل، فلا زكاة على صبي، وقال المؤلف في الحاشية : لا زكاة على المجنون، إذا جن السنة كلها فإذا أفاق بعض الحول اختلفوا فيه، والصحيح عند الإمام اشتراط الإفاقة أول السنة لإنعقاد الحول وآخرها ليخاطب بالأداء وتمامه فيها
His statement: 'upon a free person' excludes the slave and his like. His statement: 'Muslim' excludes the disbeliever, even an apostate, on the basis that he is not addressed with the branches of Shari'ah; if an apostate becomes Muslim, he is not addressed with any of the acts of worship during his apostasy, and if he apostatized after their obligation, they lapse. His statement: 'mature' (mukallaf) i.e., adult, sane; there is no zakat upon a minor. The author said in the Hashiya: There is no zakat upon the insane if he is insane the entire year. If he becomes sane during part of the year, they differ. The correct view according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) is to require sanity at the beginning of the year for the year to commence and at its end to be addressed with payment, and its completion is in it.
Source pages p. 714

Commentary
This passage lays out three conditions for the person obligated to pay zakat: freedom (not a slave), Islam (not a disbeliever or apostate during apostasy), and legal capacity (mukallaf: adult and sane). Slaves, disbelievers, and minors are not obligated. For the insane, the ruling is detailed: if insane the entire year, no zakat is due; but if sanity returns during the year, the correct Hanafi position requires sanity at both the start (for the year to begin) and end (for the obligation to pay) of the lunar year. This is an intra-Hanafi difference that is resolved by Imam Abu Hanifa's position.

Key Terms
مكلف (mukallaf): A person who has reached legal maturity (baligh) and is sane ('aqil), thus addressed by divine commands.
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate from Islam; during apostasy, not addressed with acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when must an insane person be sane for zakat to be obligatory?
A) At the beginning and end of the lunar year
B) At the end of the year only
C) At the middle of the year
D) At the time of payment only

Key Takeaway
Zakat is obligatory only on free, Muslim, adult, sane persons; for the insane, sanity at both start and end of the year is required.

Conditions for Zakat on Property: Nisab, Ownership, Debts, Needs, Growth, and Year
Commentary on conditions for zakat on property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for zakat on property and apply the Hanafi ruling that gold/silver jewelry is zakatable and that cash held for expenses is also subject to zakat.

Core Idea
Gold and silver are inherently zakatable; cash for expenses is not exempt despite an intra-Hanafi difference.

This commentary from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the prerequisites for zakat on wealth. It details what counts as owned nisab, the exemption for basic needs and debts, and the critical distinction between actual and potential growth. It also resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether cash set aside for daily expenses is zakatable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions for zakat obligation
List the conditions mentioned: complete ownership of nisab, freedom from debt, freedom from basic needs, growth (actual or potential), completion of one lunar year, and that the property be of a zakatable type (gold, silver, trade goods, grazing livestock).
The passage groups these under the phrase 'مالك لنصاب فارغ عن الدين وعن حاجته الأصلية نام ولو تقديراً'.
2
Analyze the ruling on jewelry
Note that all gold and silver jewelry is zakatable regardless of its use (even a man's silver ring or woman's bracelet) because these metals are inherently 'prices' (thumniyya). This is based on the fact that they are created as mediums of exchange.
The text cites 'خلقا أثماناً' (they are created as prices) as the reasoning.
3
Examine the exemption for basic needs and debts
Identify what counts as basic needs (clothing, housing, tools, books for scholars, etc.) and debts (including deferred debts like dowry, but not guarantees without claim). Property set aside for these is exempt from zakat even if held for a year.
There is a distinction: 'دين' (debt) that is due vs. 'كفالة' (guarantee) that is not yet claimed.
4
Understand growth: actual vs. potential
Actual growth comes from trade, breeding, etc. Potential growth (nama taqdiri) means the property is capable of growth, e.g., it is in the owner's control and can be invested. This is sufficient for zakat obligation.
This is a Hanafi view; Shafi'is require actual growth.
5
Resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute on cash for expenses
Some sources (al-Mi'raj, al-Bada'i) say cash held for expenses is zakatable, while others exempt it. The author notes that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that zakat is obligatory on cash however held, as per al-Durr and al-Haskafi.
This is a critical refinement: the text first states an exemption, then corrects it with the stronger opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله مالك لنصاب دخل فيه ما ملكه بسبب خبيث كمغصوب خلطه إلا إذا كان له غيره منفصل عنه يوفي دينه ،در، ولا بد أن يكون الملك تاماً فخرج ما ملكه المكاتب. قوله: (أو حلياً) وهو ما يتحلى به من الذهب والفضة سواء كان مباح الاستعمال، أولاً، ولو خاتم الفضة للرجل، وسوار اليد للمرأة أفاده صاحب الدرر وفي الدر أفاد وجوب الزكاة في النقدين، ولو كانا للتجمل، أو للنفقة قال : لأنهما خلقا أثماناً فيزكيهما كيف كانا قوله: (أو ما يساوي قيمته الأولى أو ما يساويه قيمة والضمير يرجع إلى النصاب لأن النصاب يقوم به، ولا يتقوم قوله: (فارغ من (الذين) أي الذي له مطالب من جهة العباد سواء كان الله كزكاة وخراج أو للعبد، ولو كفالة أو مؤجلاً، ولو صداق زوجته المؤجل بخلاف دین وكفالة لعدم المطالب وعروض الدين كالهلاك عند محمد، ورجحه في البحر. قوله: (وعن حاجته (الأصلية) كثيابه المحتاج إليها لدفع الحر والبرد، وكالنفقة ودور السكني وآلات الحرب، والحرفة وأساس المنزل، ودواب الركوب، وكتب العلم لأهلها فإذا كان عنده دراهم أعدها لهذه الأشياء، وحال عليها الحول لا تجب فيها الزكاة، وكتب العلم لغير أهلها ليست من الحوائج الأصلية، وإن كانت الزكاة لا تجب على صاحبها بدون نية التجارة بحر بتصرف، وقوله : وكالنفقة لا زكاة فيها، ولو حال عليها الحول قال فيه : وهو مخالف لما في المعراج والبدائع أن الزكاة تجب في النقد كيف أمسكه للنفقة، أو للنماء ا هـ. قوله : (نام ولو تقديراً) والنماء الحقيقي يكون بالتوالد والتناسل والتجارات والتقديري يكون بالتمكن من الاستنماء بأن يكون في يده أو يد نائبه در قوله وشرط وجوب (أدائها أي افتراضها قوله : (حولان الحول) وهو في ملكه أي وثمنية المال كالدراهم والدنانير، أو السوم أو نية التجارة في العروض. قوله : (إلى مجانسه) النقدان في الزكاة جنس واحد فما استفاده من أحدهما يضم إلى ما عنده منهما وما استفاده السائمة يضم إليها لا إليهما قوله : (أو غيره كهبة ووصية.
His statement: 'owner of a nisab' includes what he owns through a corrupt cause, such as mixed usurped property, unless he has another separate property to pay his debt. And the ownership must be complete, thus the property of a mukatab is excluded. His statement: 'or jewelry' – it is what is worn as adornment from gold and silver, whether its use is permissible or not, even a silver ring for a man, and a bracelet for a woman. The author of al-Durar narrated from al-Durr the obligation of zakat in gold and silver even if they are for adornment or for expenses, because they are created as prices; so one pays zakat on them however they are. His statement: 'or what equals its value' – the pronoun refers to the nisab, because the nisab is valued by it. His statement: 'free from debt' – meaning from that which has claims from the side of people, whether it is for Allah like zakat and kharaj, or for a slave (i.e., a human creditor), even if it is a guarantee or deferred, even the deferred dowry of his wife, unlike a debt of guarantee because there is no claim; and a debt of commodities is like destruction according to Muhammad, and he preferred it in al-Bahr. His statement: 'and from his basic needs' – such as his clothes needed to repel heat and cold, and expenses, dwellings, weapons, tools, the foundation of the house, riding animals, and books of knowledge for their owners. So if he has dirhams set aside for these things and a year passes over them, zakat is not due. But books of knowledge for non-owners are not from basic needs, though zakat is not due on their owner without the intention of trade. And his statement: 'and expenses' – no zakat in them even if a year passes over them. He said: This contradicts what is in al-Mi'raj and al-Bada'i that zakat is obligatory on cash however he holds it for expenses or for growth. His statement: 'growing even if only potentially' – actual growth is through procreation, breeding, and trades; potential growth is through having the ability to make it grow, by it being in his hand or the hand of his agent. His statement: 'and a condition of the obligation of its payment' – i.e., its being made obligatory. His statement: 'the completion of the year' – while it is in his ownership, i.e., the 'thumniyya' of the property like dirhams and dinars, or grazing, or intention of trade in commodities. His statement: 'to its like' – gold and silver are one kind in zakat; so what he acquires from one is added to what he has from both, and what he acquires from grazing animals is added to them, not to them. His statement: 'or other than it' like gift and bequest.
Source pages p. 714

Commentary
This extensive passage covers multiple conditions related to the property on which zakat is due. First, the nisab must be owned completely; even property acquired through corrupt means (like usurped goods) is subject to zakat if a separate lawful property exists to pay debts. Jewelry of gold and silver is zakatable regardless of its use (even a man's silver ring or woman's bracelet) because these metals are inherently 'prices' (thamaniyya). Trade goods of equivalent value also count. The wealth must be free from debts (including deferred debts like dowry, but not debts without claim like kafala) and free from basic necessities (like clothing, housing, tools, books of knowledge for scholars). There is an intra-Hanafi difference on whether cash set aside for expenses is zakatable: some sources say yes, but the author notes a contradiction. Growth can be actual (trade, breeding) or potential (the wealth is capable of growth). Finally, one lunar year must pass while the nisab remains owned, and gains during the year are added to the nisab of the same kind (e.g., gold to gold, livestock to livestock).

Key Terms
حلية (hilya): Jewelry from gold and silver, whether permissible or not in use.
ثمنية (thumniyya): The quality of being a price (medium of exchange), inherent in gold and silver.
نماء تقديري (nama' taqdiri): Potential growth; the ability to produce profit even if not currently doing so.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zakat is due only if used for trade
B) Zakat is due on all forms, even if for personal use
C) Zakat is due only on women's jewelry
D) Zakat is not due on jewelry at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates zakat on all gold and silver jewelry and on cash regardless of its intended use (expenses or growth), based on the intrinsic thumniyya of these metals and the sufficiency of potential growth.

Accelerating Zakat (Ta'jil) in the Hanafi School
Commentary on the permissibility and conditions of paying zakat in advance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid ta'jil and apply them to determine whether an advance zakat payment is valid.

Core Idea
Ta'jil is valid only if the payer already has nisab at payment; later recipient changes don't invalidate.

Paying zakat before the year completes—known as ta'jil—is a permitted practice in the Hanafi school, but it is not unconditional. This lesson examines the classical ruling from al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its commentary, clarifying the precise requirements for a valid advance payment. Understanding these conditions prevents common errors in zakat calculation and ensures that the payer fulfills their obligation correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is paying zakat in advance (ta'jil). The ruling is permissibility (sunnah muakkadah) under specific conditions. Note that it is not obligatory; the obligation arises only after the year completes.
The text uses 'ja'iz' (permissible) but the Hanafi classification often grades it as sunnah muakkadah.
2
Extract conditions from the example
The example: one has 300 dirhams, pays 100 dirhams as zakat for 200 dirhams over 20 years. This is valid because the payer already possesses the nisab (200 dirhams) at the time of payment. The key condition is that the payer must have the full nisab at the moment of advancing the payment.
3
Understand the negative condition
If the payer does not have the nisab at the time of payment (e.g., he has less than 200 dirhams but pays advance zakat for 200), the payment is invalid even if his wealth later reaches the nisab by year-end.
This is a crucial distinction: possession of nisab at payment time is a prerequisite.
4
Analyze the stability condition
Two additional conditions: (1) the entire nisab must not be cut off (i.e., completely lost) during the year—partial reduction is acceptable; (2) the nisab must be complete at the end of the year for the payment to count for that year.
If the nisab is completely lost mid-year, the advance payment becomes invalid because the obligation never materialized.
5
Evaluate the recipient change rule
If the recipient becomes wealthy, dies, or apostatizes after receiving the payment but before the year ends, the payment remains valid. The criterion for eligibility is the recipient's status at the time of payment, not later.
This is a practical ruling that protects the payer from invalidation due to unforeseen changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو من عجل ذو نصاب لسنين صح صورته له ثلثمائة درهم دفع منها مائة عن المائتين لعشرين سنة جاز بشرط أن يكون عنده النصاب الذي عجل عنه كما في الصورة، فلو كان في ملكه أقل منه فعجل خمسة عن مائتين، وتم الحول والنصاب تام لا يجوز، وأن لا ينقطع جميع النصاب أثناء الحول، وأن يكون النصاب كاملاً . آخر الحول، وتمامه في كتابة الدر فلو عجل الفقير فأيسر قبل تمام الحول، أو مات أو ارتد أجزاء لأن المعتبر كونه مصرفاً وقت الصرف إليه لا بعده در
His statement: 'even if he who possesses a nisab accelerates (zakat) for years, it is valid.' Its form: he has three hundred dirhams, he pays one hundred from them for two hundred for twenty years; it is permissible on condition that he has the nisab which he is accelerating for, as in the example. If he has less than it (the nisab) in his possession and he accelerates five for two hundred, and the year completes and the nisab is complete, it is not permissible. And that the entire nisab does not become cut off during the year, and that the nisab is complete at the end of the year. Its completion is in the writing of al-Durr. If the poor person (recipient) becomes wealthy before the completion of the year, or dies, or apostatizes, it suffices because consideration is given to his being a valid recipient at the time of payment, not afterwards.
Source pages p. 715

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on paying zakat in advance (ta'jil). It is valid if the payer already possesses the nisab that he is accelerating the zakat for. The example: one has 300 dirhams and pays 100 in advance for the zakat on 200 for 20 years. However, if he pays before having the nisab, it is invalid. Conditions: the nisab must not be cut off during the year, and it must be complete at the end of the year. If the recipient becomes wealthy, dies, or apostatizes before the year ends, the payment is still valid because the condition of eligibility is based on the time of payment, not later. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jil): Paying zakat before the completion of the lunar year.
مصرف (masraf): Eligible recipient of zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a zakat recipient becomes wealthy before the year ends after receiving advance zakat?
A) The zakat payment is invalid and must be repeated
B) The zakat payment remains valid
C) The payer must take back the zakat
D) The zakat becomes sadaqah instead

Key Takeaway
Accelerating zakat is valid if the payer has the nisab at payment, the nisab remains uncut during the year and is complete at year-end; later recipient status changes do not affect the payment.

Zakat on Debts: Strong Category (Qawi)
Commentary defining strong debt for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of debts for zakat and determine which debts qualify as strong (qawi) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Only strong debts impose zakat for past years upon receipt.

In the Hanafi school, not all debts are treated equally when it comes to zakat. Debts are classified into strong, medium, and weak based on the likelihood of collection. This passage introduces the strong category, which includes loans and trade prices that the debtor acknowledges or for which the creditor has evidence. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly calculating zakat on wealth that is owed to you.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State clearly that this passage deals with the obligation of zakat on debts (zakat al-dayn). The ruling is not a blanket rule; it depends on the debt's category.
Zakat on debts is wajib, but details vary by category.
2
List the three categories
The passage mentions that debt is divided into strong (qawi), medium (wasat), and weak (da'if). Focus here on the strong category.
Medium and weak are not detailed in this passage.
3
Define strong debt
Strong debt includes two types: (1) the principal of a loan (badal al-qard), and (2) the price of trade goods sold on credit (mal al-tijarah). For both, the debtor must either acknowledge the debt or evidence must exist against a denier.
The condition 'muqir' (acknowledger) or 'jāḥid ʿalayhi bayyinah' (denier with evidence) is essential.
4
Understand the zakat implication
For strong debts, when the creditor finally receives the payment, he must pay zakat on that amount for all the past years since the debt was incurred. This is because the debt is considered effectively in his possession due to the debtor's acknowledgment or evidence.
Intra-Hanafi details: Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn have differences on some nuances, but the ruling stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزكاة الدين على أقسام فإنه قوي ووسط وضعيف فالقوي، وهو بدل القرض، ومال التجارة إذا قبضه وكان على مقر ولو مفلساً، أو على جاحد عليه بينة
And the zakat on debt is divided into categories: strong, medium, and weak. The strong one is the substitute of a loan (qard) and trade goods when he receives it, and it is against an acknowledgee (muqir) even if bankrupt, or against a denier who has evidence against him.
Source pages p. 715

Commentary
This passage introduces the classification of debts in relation to zakat. The Hanafi school divides debts into three categories: strong (qawi), medium (wasat), and weak (da'if). The strong category includes loans (qard) and the price of trade goods that have been sold, when the creditor actually receives the payment. It also includes debts that the debtor acknowledges (muqir) even if he is insolvent, or debts from a denier but the creditor has evidence. For strong debts, zakat is due on the amount when received for the past years. The text is cut off, so further details on medium and weak are not included in this passage.

Key Terms
بدل القرض (badal al-qard): The principal of a loan that is due to be repaid.
مال التجارة (mal al-tijarah): The price of trade goods sold on credit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a strong debt?
A) A loan that the debtor denies with no evidence
B) A loan that the debtor acknowledges even if bankrupt
C) A deferred dowry from a divorce
D) A debt that is doubtful

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, strong debts (loans and trade prices that are acknowledged or evidenced) require zakat for all past years upon receipt.

Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner
8 min
Zakat on Newly Acquired Assets (Mustafad)
Ruling on mustafad with commentary on jins and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mustafad and explain how it is added to similar existing assets for zakat calculation.

Core Idea
Newly acquired assets during the zakat year are added to their type and zakat is due at the end of the original year.

When a person acquires new wealth during the zakat year, the question arises whether it requires a new year or joins the existing year. This lesson covers the Hanafi rule: mustafad is added to similar assets (e.g., gold to gold) and zakat is paid at the end of the original year, regardless of the source of acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is acquiring new property (mustafad) during the zakat year. The ruling is that it is added to the same type of existing assets and zakat is due at the end of the original year.
2
Understand the condition of similarity
The new asset must be of the same jins (type) as existing zakatable assets. For example, gold and silver are considered one type.
An exception: mustafad from grazing livestock is added to livestock, not to cash.
3
Note the source of acquisition
Whether acquired by trade, inheritance, gift, or bequest, the ruling is the same.
4
Apply the rule to practical cases
If you have 200 dirhams of silver and receive 50 dirhams as a gift mid-year, you add the 50 to the 200 and pay zakat on 250 at the end of the year.

Book of Zakat. The original (asset); as for what is acquired during the year, it is added to its similar type and zakat is paid at completion of the original year, whether acquired by trade, inheritance, or otherwise. And if a possessor of nisab advances zakat for years, it is valid. A condition for the validity of its payment is intention concurrent with its payment to the poor, or his agent, or for setting aside what is obligatory, even if it is a constructive concurrence, as if he paid without intention then intended while the property still exists in the hand of the poor. And it is not a condition that the poor person knows it is zakat according to the soundest view, so that if he gave him something and called it a gift or a loan and intended it as zakat, it is valid. And if he gave charity with all his property and did not intend zakat, the obligation of zakat drops from him. Zakat on debt has categories: strong, medium, and weak. The strong is the substitute of a loan and trade goods when he receives it and it is against an acknowledging debtor even if insolvent, or against a denying debtor with evidence. ... (continues with detailed commentary on various points including conditions of advance payment, intention, debt categories, and mal al-dhimar).
Source pages p. 715

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive hashiyah (super-commentary) on the rulings of zakat from Maraqi al-Falah. It opens with the ruling on newly acquired assets during the zakat year: they are added to the same type of existing assets (e.g., gold to gold, silver to silver), and zakat is due at the end of the original year, regardless of whether the asset was acquired through trade, inheritance, or other means. The commentary then discusses the permissibility of advancing zakat payment before it is due: a person with nisab can pay zakat for multiple years in advance, subject to conditions such as having the nisab at the time of payment and at the end of each year, and that the nisab does not completely disappear during the year. The next section covers the conditions for valid zakat payment: intention must be present at the time of payment, either actual or constructive (e.g., paying without intention then intending while the money is still in the poor person's hand). The poor person need not know it is zakat; if the giver calls it a gift or loan but intends zakat, it is valid. If someone gives all his wealth as charity without intending zakat, his zakat obligation is dropped. The passage then classifies debts into three types for zakat purposes: 'strong' (e.g., loan receivables, trade debts where the debtor acknowledges or has evidence), 'medium' (e.g., price of non-trade items like used clothes, which require receipt of nisab and consideration of past year), and 'weak' (e.g., dowry, inheritance, blood money, which require receipt and a full year after receipt according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad make zakat due proportionally on what is received). Finally, the text discusses 'mal al-dhimar' (lost or inaccessible property) such as runaway slaves, lost items, or property seized unjustly, for which no zakat is due for past years; zakat begins only after recovery and the passage of a full year. The commentary by al-Tahtawi provides detailed clarifications on each point, citing sources and resolving contradictions.

Key Terms
مستفاد (mustafād): Property newly acquired during the zakat year, which is added to similar existing assets for zakat calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on mustafad acquired by inheritance?
A) It requires a separate new zakat year.
B) It is added to similar existing assets and zakat is due at the end of the original year.
C) Zakat is not due on inherited wealth.
D) It is added only if it is cash.

Key Takeaway
Mustafad is added to the same type of existing zakatable assets and zakat is due at the end of the original year.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate

Advance Payment of Zakat (Ta'jil)
Ruling on advance payment of zakat with conditions and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid advance payment of zakat for multiple years and apply them to a scenario.

Core Idea
Zakat can be paid in advance for many years, provided the nisab remains intact at the end of each year and the recipient is eligible at the time of payment.

Can you pay zakat early for future years? The Hanafi school permits this, but with strict conditions. This lesson explores the ruling from the text, including the critical requirement that the payer must have the full nisab at the time of payment and at each year-end, and that the recipient must be eligible at the time of payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Advancing zakat for multiple years is valid (sahih) for a person who possesses nisab.
2
List the conditions for validity
1. The payer must have the nisab at the time of advance payment. 2. The nisab must not be completely exhausted during the intervening years. 3. The nisab must be complete at the end of each year.
Example from text: 300 dirhams, paying 100 for 20 years.
3
Note the effect on recipient
If the recipient becomes rich, dies, or apostatizes before the end of the year, the payment is still valid because eligibility is assessed at the time of payment.
4
Apply to a case
If a person has 300 dirhams and pays 100 zakat for 20 years in advance, it is valid only if he still has 300 dirhams at each year-end (the nisab for which he advanced).

إلا إذا نص على التفويض، ولو دفعها المعلم إلى خليفته إن كان بحيث يعمل له لو لم يعطه صح، وإلا لا در قوله : ( ولم ينو الزكاة ولا نذراً، ولا واجباً آخر فإذا نواهما يضمن الزكاة، ولو تصدق ببعضه لم تسقط حصته عند الثاني خلافاً للثالث، واعلم أن أداء الدين عن ا المال الذي يصح، والحيلة أن يعطي المديون زكاته ثم يأخذها عن دينه، ولو امتنع المديون مد زكاة لما مضى ويتراخى وجوب الأداء إلى أن يقبض أربعين درهماً فقيها درهم لأن ما دون الخمس من النصاب عفو لا زكاة فيه صح وكذا فيما زاد ،بحسابه، والوسط وهو بدل ما ليس للتجارة كثمن ثياب البذلة، وعبد الخدمة، ودار السكنى لا تجب الزكاة فيه ما لم يقبض نصاباً، ويعتبر لما Book of Zakat. The original (asset); as for what is acquired during the year, it is added to its similar type and zakat is paid at completion of the original year, whether acquired by trade, inheritance, or otherwise. And if a possessor of nisab advances zakat for years, it is valid. A condition for the validity of its payment is intention concurrent with its payment to the poor, or his agent, or for setting aside what is obligatory, even if it is a constructive concurrence, as if he paid without intention then intended while the property still exists in the hand of the poor. And it is not a condition that the poor person knows it is zakat according to the soundest view, so that if he gave him something and called it a gift or a loan and intended it as zakat, it is valid. And if he gave charity with all his property and did not intend zakat, the obligation of zakat drops from him. Zakat on debt has categories: strong, medium, and weak. The strong is the substitute of a loan and trade goods when he receives it and it is against an acknowledging debtor even if insolvent, or against a denying debtor with evidence. ... (continues with detailed commentary on various points including conditions of advance payment, intention, debt categories, and mal al-dhimar).
Source pages p. 715

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive hashiyah (super-commentary) on the rulings of zakat from Maraqi al-Falah. It opens with the ruling on newly acquired assets during the zakat year: they are added to the same type of existing assets (e.g., gold to gold, silver to silver), and zakat is due at the end of the original year, regardless of whether the asset was acquired through trade, inheritance, or other means. The commentary then discusses the permissibility of advancing zakat payment before it is due: a person with nisab can pay zakat for multiple years in advance, subject to conditions such as having the nisab at the time of payment and at the end of each year, and that the nisab does not completely disappear during the year. The next section covers the conditions for valid zakat payment: intention must be present at the time of payment, either actual or constructive (e.g., paying without intention then intending while the money is still in the poor person's hand). The poor person need not know it is zakat; if the giver calls it a gift or loan but intends zakat, it is valid. If someone gives all his wealth as charity without intending zakat, his zakat obligation is dropped. The passage then classifies debts into three types for zakat purposes: 'strong' (e.g., loan receivables, trade debts where the debtor acknowledges or has evidence), 'medium' (e.g., price of non-trade items like used clothes, which require receipt of nisab and consideration of past year), and 'weak' (e.g., dowry, inheritance, blood money, which require receipt and a full year after receipt according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad make zakat due proportionally on what is received). Finally, the text discusses 'mal al-dhimar' (lost or inaccessible property) such as runaway slaves, lost items, or property seized unjustly, for which no zakat is due for past years; zakat begins only after recovery and the passage of a full year. The commentary by al-Tahtawi provides detailed clarifications on each point, citing sources and resolving contradictions.

Key Terms
تعجيل الزكاة (ta'jīl al-zakāh): Advancing zakat payment before it is due for future years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person pays zakat for 5 years in advance but loses the nisab during the first year, what happens?
A) All advance payments are invalid.
B) The first year's payment is valid; subsequent years become invalid.
C) The entire advance is still valid because intention was there.
D) The payer must repay the advance for the first year.

Key Takeaway
Advance zakat is valid only if the payer maintains the nisab at each year-end.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Intention (Niyyah) for Zakat Payment
Ruling on intention conditions in zakat with examples of constructive intention and charity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions and implications of intention in zakat, including constructive intention and the effect of not intending zakat.

Core Idea
Intention must be present at payment; it can be constructive if the property is still with the recipient, and the recipient need not know it is zakat.

The validity of zakat payment hinges on intention. This lesson examines the Hanafi rules: intention must coincide with payment (actual or constructive), the recipient's knowledge is not required, and if one gives away all wealth as charity without intending zakat, the obligation drops. The commentary provides examples like paying without intention then intending while the money is still in the poor's hand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of intention
Intention (niyyah) must be concurrent with the payment or with setting aside the zakat amount.
It can be actual (at the moment of giving) or constructive (e.g., paying without intention, then intending while the money is still with the poor).
2
Understand constructive intention
If someone pays without intention but later intends while the money is still in the hand of the poor, the zakat is valid. This is called 'constructive concurrence' (muqāranah ḥukmiyyah).
3
Note that recipient's knowledge is not required
The poor person does not need to know the payment is zakat. If the giver calls it a gift or loan but intends zakat, it is valid.
4
Recognize the ruling on general charity
If someone gives all his wealth as charity without intending zakat, the obligation of zakat for that year drops. But if he intended something else (like a vow), he must still pay zakat.

Book of Zakat. The original (asset); as for what is acquired during the year, it is added to its similar type and zakat is paid at completion of the original year, whether acquired by trade, inheritance, or otherwise. And if a possessor of nisab advances zakat for years, it is valid. A condition for the validity of its payment is intention concurrent with its payment to the poor, or his agent, or for setting aside what is obligatory, even if it is a constructive concurrence, as if he paid without intention then intended while the property still exists in the hand of the poor. And it is not a condition that the poor person knows it is zakat according to the soundest view, so that if he gave him something and called it a gift or a loan and intended it as zakat, it is valid. And if he gave charity with all his property and did not intend zakat, the obligation of zakat drops from him. Zakat on debt has categories: strong, medium, and weak. The strong is the substitute of a loan and trade goods when he receives it and it is against an acknowledging debtor even if insolvent, or against a denying debtor with evidence. ... (continues with detailed commentary on various points including conditions of advance payment, intention, debt categories, and mal al-dhimar).
Source pages p. 715

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive hashiyah (super-commentary) on the rulings of zakat from Maraqi al-Falah. It opens with the ruling on newly acquired assets during the zakat year: they are added to the same type of existing assets (e.g., gold to gold, silver to silver), and zakat is due at the end of the original year, regardless of whether the asset was acquired through trade, inheritance, or other means. The commentary then discusses the permissibility of advancing zakat payment before it is due: a person with nisab can pay zakat for multiple years in advance, subject to conditions such as having the nisab at the time of payment and at the end of each year, and that the nisab does not completely disappear during the year. The next section covers the conditions for valid zakat payment: intention must be present at the time of payment, either actual or constructive (e.g., paying without intention then intending while the money is still in the poor person's hand). The poor person need not know it is zakat; if the giver calls it a gift or loan but intends zakat, it is valid. If someone gives all his wealth as charity without intending zakat, his zakat obligation is dropped. The passage then classifies debts into three types for zakat purposes: 'strong' (e.g., loan receivables, trade debts where the debtor acknowledges or has evidence), 'medium' (e.g., price of non-trade items like used clothes, which require receipt of nisab and consideration of past year), and 'weak' (e.g., dowry, inheritance, blood money, which require receipt and a full year after receipt according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad make zakat due proportionally on what is received). Finally, the text discusses 'mal al-dhimar' (lost or inaccessible property) such as runaway slaves, lost items, or property seized unjustly, for which no zakat is due for past years; zakat begins only after recovery and the passage of a full year. The commentary by al-Tahtawi provides detailed clarifications on each point, citing sources and resolving contradictions.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention of the giver to pay zakat, required for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person pays zakat without any intention but later intends while the money is still with the poor, the zakat is:
A) Invalid because intention was missing at payment.
B) Valid because of constructive intention.
C) Valid only if the poor person is informed later.
D) Invalid unless the money is returned and given again with intention.

Key Takeaway
Zakat intention can be actual or constructive; the poor person's knowledge is not required.

Zakat on Debts: Strong, Medium, and Weak Categories
Ruling on zakat for different categories of debts with internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify debts into strong, medium, and weak categories and apply the corresponding zakat ruling.

Core Idea
Debts are categorized; strong debts require zakat upon receipt, weak debts require a new year after receipt, and medium debts are treated like weak in the soundest narration.

Not all debts are treated the same in zakat. The Hanafi school classifies debts into three grades based on certainty and growth. This lesson unpacks each category, from loan receivables (strong) to dowry and inheritance (weak), and the practical differences in calculating zakat.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three categories
Strong (qawī): loan returns and trade debts where the debtor acknowledges or there is evidence. Medium (wasaṭ): price of non-trade items like used clothes. Weak (ḍaʻīf): non-monetary items like dowry, inheritance, blood money, etc.
2
Apply ruling for strong debts
When received, zakat is due immediately for the past years without requiring a new year? The text says: for strong debts, zakat is due when received, but it does not require a new year; it seems zakat is calculated for past years? Actually the passage states: 'لا تجب الزكاة فيه ما لم يقبض نصاباً'? Let's read carefully. It says for strong: 'إذا قبضه وكان على مقر...' The ruling is that zakat is due when received even if the debtor is insolvent. For medium and weak, zakat is due only after receipt of nisab and a year after receipt according to Abu Hanifa.
The text has a dispute between Imam and Sahibayn for weak debts.
3
Apply ruling for medium debts
No zakat until one receives nisab and considers the past year (in the sound narration). Imam Abu Hanifa says no zakat until receipt and a full year after. Sahibayn say zakat is due proportionally for past years.
4
Apply ruling for weak debts
No zakat until receipt of nisab and a full year after receipt according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Sahibayn hold that zakat is due on what is received proportionally for past years.
The mufta bihi is Imam's view.

Book of Zakat. The original (asset); as for what is acquired during the year, it is added to its similar type and zakat is paid at completion of the original year, whether acquired by trade, inheritance, or otherwise. And if a possessor of nisab advances zakat for years, it is valid. A condition for the validity of its payment is intention concurrent with its payment to the poor, or his agent, or for setting aside what is obligatory, even if it is a constructive concurrence, as if he paid without intention then intended while the property still exists in the hand of the poor. And it is not a condition that the poor person knows it is zakat according to the soundest view, so that if he gave him something and called it a gift or a loan and intended it as zakat, it is valid. And if he gave charity with all his property and did not intend zakat, the obligation of zakat drops from him. Zakat on debt has categories: strong, medium, and weak. The strong is the substitute of a loan and trade goods when he receives it and it is against an acknowledging debtor even if insolvent, or against a denying debtor with evidence. ... (continues with detailed commentary on various points including conditions of advance payment, intention, debt categories, and mal al-dhimar).
Source pages p. 715

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive hashiyah (super-commentary) on the rulings of zakat from Maraqi al-Falah. It opens with the ruling on newly acquired assets during the zakat year: they are added to the same type of existing assets (e.g., gold to gold, silver to silver), and zakat is due at the end of the original year, regardless of whether the asset was acquired through trade, inheritance, or other means. The commentary then discusses the permissibility of advancing zakat payment before it is due: a person with nisab can pay zakat for multiple years in advance, subject to conditions such as having the nisab at the time of payment and at the end of each year, and that the nisab does not completely disappear during the year. The next section covers the conditions for valid zakat payment: intention must be present at the time of payment, either actual or constructive (e.g., paying without intention then intending while the money is still in the poor person's hand). The poor person need not know it is zakat; if the giver calls it a gift or loan but intends zakat, it is valid. If someone gives all his wealth as charity without intending zakat, his zakat obligation is dropped. The passage then classifies debts into three types for zakat purposes: 'strong' (e.g., loan receivables, trade debts where the debtor acknowledges or has evidence), 'medium' (e.g., price of non-trade items like used clothes, which require receipt of nisab and consideration of past year), and 'weak' (e.g., dowry, inheritance, blood money, which require receipt and a full year after receipt according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad make zakat due proportionally on what is received). Finally, the text discusses 'mal al-dhimar' (lost or inaccessible property) such as runaway slaves, lost items, or property seized unjustly, for which no zakat is due for past years; zakat begins only after recovery and the passage of a full year. The commentary by al-Tahtawi provides detailed clarifications on each point, citing sources and resolving contradictions.

Key Terms
دين قوي (dayn qawī): A strong debt, such as a loan or trade price owed by an acknowledging debtor, on which zakat is due when received.
دين وسط (dayn wasaṭ): A medium debt, such as the price of non-trade items, requiring receipt of nisab and consideration of past year (sound narration).
دين ضعيف (dayn ḍaʻīf): A weak debt, such as dowry, inheritance, blood money, for which zakat requires receipt and a full year after receipt (Imam Abu Hanifa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when is zakat due on a weak debt like unpaid dowry?
A) Immediately upon receipt, with zakat calculated for the past years.
B) After one full year from receipt, on the amount received.
C) No zakat is due because dowry is not zakatable.
D) Based on the intention of the creditor.

Key Takeaway
Debts are categorized; weak debts require a new year after receipt according to the mufta bihi.

Zakat on Inaccessible Property (Mal al-Dhimar)
Ruling on mal al-dhimar with examples and a point of ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mal al-dhimar and state the ruling that no zakat is due for past years upon recovery.

Core Idea
Inaccessible property (mal al-dhimar) incurs no zakat for past years; zakat begins after recovery and a full year.

What if you have property that is completely out of reach, like a runaway slave, a lost item, or money seized unjustly? The Hanafi school rules that no zakat is due for the years it was inaccessible. Once recovered, a new zakat year starts. This lesson defines mal al-dhimar and lists its examples from the text.

Guided Path
1
Define mal al-dhimar
Property that is impossible to access despite ownership, such as a runaway slave, lost item, property seized unjustly, buried and forgotten treasure, etc.
2
State the ruling
No zakat is due for the past years during which the property was inaccessible. Zakat becomes due only after recovery and the passage of one full lunar year.
3
Identify examples from the text
Examples: runaway slave (ābiq), lost property (mafqūd), seized property without evidence (maghsūb), buried treasure with forgotten location, money taken by a tyrant (musādara), etc.
4
Note the exception
If the owner has evidence of the seizure (like a court order), the property is not considered dhimar and zakat may be due for past years? The text mentions a dispute: some say if there is evidence, zakat is due; others say still no zakat because evidence may not be accepted.

فقيها درهم لأن ما دون الخمس من النصاب عفو لا زكاة فيه صح وكذا فيما زاد ،بحسابه، والوسط وهو بدل ما ليس للتجارة كثمن ثياب البذلة، وعبد الخدمة، ودار السكنى لا تجب الزكاة فيه ما لم يقبض نصاباً، ويعتبر لما وهذا عند الإمام، وأوجبا عن المقبوض من الديون الثلاثة بحسابه مطلقاً، وإذا قبض مال الضمار لا تجب زكاة السنين الماضية وهو كآبق ومفقود ومغصوب ليس عليه بنية، ومال ساقط في ومدفون في مفازة، أو دار عظيمة وقد نسي مكانه، ومأخوذ مصادرة ومودع عند من لا يعرفه، وأخذها لكونه لا ظفر بجنس حقه فإن مانعه رفعه للقاضي قوله: (أو على جاحد عليه بينة) تبع فيه العيني، وفي النهر عن الخانية والتحفة صحح قول محمد بعدم الوجوب فيه لأن كل بينة لا تقبل، ولا كل قاض يعدل قوله : ففيها درهم هذا إنما يظهر إذا كان الماضي عاماً واحداً. قوله : (لأن ما دون الخ) علة لقوله : ويتراخى وجوب الأداء إلى أن يقبض أربعين درهماً. قوله: (وكذا وصار ثمنها ديناً في ذمة المشتري حتى حال عليه الحول، فالحكم ما ذكره، ومثله يقال : فيما بعده. قوله: (والوصية) إذا تأخرت عند الوارث مثلاً عاماً قوله : ( وبدل الخلع إذا تأخر عند الزوجة عاماً. قوله: (والصلح عن دم العمد إذا تأخر بدله عند القاتل عاماً مثلاً قوله : (والدية) إذا تأخرت عند العاقلة، أو القاتل عاماً مثلاً ثم قبضها ولي الدم قوله (والسعاية) كما إذا أعتق بعضه، واستسعاه في البعض الآخر،
