باب صدقة الفطر لفظ إسلامي والفطرة مولد وأمر بها في السنة التي فرض فيها رمضان قبل الزكاة، وكان يخطب قبل الفطر بيومين يأمر بإخراجها، ولا تسقط بهلاك المال بعد الوجوب بخلاف الزكاة. قوله : (تجب على حر مسلم) إنما وجبت لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في خطبته : «أدوا عن كل حر، وعبد صغير أو كبير نصف صاع من بر أو صاعاً من شعير أو صاعاً من تمر» أخرجه أبو داود. وتجب موسعاً في العمر عند أصحابنا، وهو الصحيح بحر كالزكاة، وقيل: مضيقاً في يوم الفطر عيناً، فبعده تكون قضاه واختاره الكمال في تحرير. ورجحه في تنوير البصائر. قوله : (مالك النصاب) اعلم أنّ النصب ثلاثة نصاب يشترط فيه النماء، وتتعلق به الزكاة، وسائر الأحكام المتعلقة بالمال النامي ونصاب تجب به أحكام أربعة حرمة الصدقة، ووجوب الأضحية، وصدقة الفطر ونفقة الأقارب، ولا يشترط فيه النمو بالتجارة، ولا حولان الحول، و نصاب تثبت به حرمة السؤال، وهو ما إذا كان عنده قوت يومه عند بعض، وقال بعضهم هو أن يملك خمسين درهماً ذكره العلامة نوح. قوله عند طلوع فجر يوم الفطر) فمن مات قبله أو ولد بعده، أو أسلم لا تجب عليه كما سيأتي. قوله: (ولم يكن للتجارة) أي وإن لم يكن للتجارة. قوله: (والمعتبر فيها) أي في حوائجه وحوائج عياله. قوله : (وأثاثه) الأثاث متاع البيت قاموس. قوله : (وإن كانوا أغنياء يخرجها من مالهم عندهما، وقال محمد: لا تجب على الصغير الغني، ومثل ما قيل في الصغير الغني يقال في المجنون الكبير الغني، والمعتوه كما في الهندية وفطرة رقيق الصغير كالصغير، وفي البحر ونفقة الطفل الغني في ماله ا هـ، ولو لم يخرج ولي الصغير والمجنون الغنيين عنهما وجب الأداء عليهما بعد البلوغ والإفاقة. قوله : (واختير أن الجد كالأب) اعلم أنهم جعلوا السبب في وجوب صدقة الفطر رأساً يموله ويلي عليه ولاية مطلقة، كما يأتي التنبيه عليه، فأورد عليه الجد، إذا كانت نوافله صغاراً في عياله لموت الأب، أو فقره حيث لا يجب عليه الإخراج في ظاهر الرواية فقد تحقق السبب، ولم تجب، وما قيل في دفع الإيراد من انتفاء السبب لأنّ الولاية غير تامة لانتقالها له من الأب، فكانت كولاية الوصي غير سديد إذا الوصي لا يموله من ماله بخلاف الجد إذا لم يكن له مال فكالأب قال الكمال : ولا مخلص عن الإيراد إلا بترجيح رواية الحسن من أنها على الجد، فصحت السببية كما ذكروه واختارها في الاختيار وجرى عليها في الدر.
Chapter of Sadaqat al-Fitr. 'Fitr' is an Islamic term, and 'fitrah' is a derived word. It was commanded in the year Ramadan was made obligatory, before zakat. He (the Prophet) used to give a sermon two days before Fitr, commanding its payment. It is not abrogated by destruction of wealth after obligation, unlike zakat. His statement: (It is obligatory upon a free Muslim). It was obligated due to his saying, peace be upon him, in his sermon: 'Pay on behalf of every free person, and slave, young or old, half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of barley or a sa' of dates.' Reported by Abu Dawud. It is obligatory broadly in the life according to our companions, and that is the correct view, like zakat. It is said: it is determined on the day of Fitr specifically; after that it would be a make-up. Al-Kamal chose this in al-Tahrir and preferred it in Tanwir al-Basa'ir. His statement: (Owner of nisab). Know that there are three nisabs: a nisab that requires growth, and zakat and other rulings related to growing wealth are attached to it; a nisab that imposes four rulings: prohibition of charity, obligation of sacrifice, Sadaqat al-Fitr, and maintenance of relatives, and growth through trade and the passing of a year are not required in it; and a nisab that establishes the prohibition of begging, which is if one has provision for one day according to some, and some said it is ownership of fifty dirhams, as mentioned by Allamah Nuh. His statement: (At the rise of dawn of the day of Fitr) Whoever dies before it or is born after it, or accepts Islam, it is not obligatory upon him as will come. His statement: (And it was not for trade) meaning even if it was not for trade. His statement: (And what is considered) meaning in his needs and the needs of his dependents. His statement: (And his furniture) al-athath is household goods. His statement: (And even if they are rich, he pays it from their wealth according to the two, and Muhammad said: It is not obligatory upon the wealthy minor. And similar to what is said about the wealthy minor, it is said about the wealthy adult insane and the imbecile as in al-Hindiyyah. And the fitrah of the slave of the minor is like the minor. And in al-Bahr: the maintenance of the wealthy child is from his wealth. And if the guardian of the wealthy minor and insane do not pay for them, it becomes obligatory on them after attaining majority and sanity. His statement: (And it was chosen that the grandfather is like the father) Know that they made the cause of obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr a head whom he supports and over whom he has absolute guardianship, as will be pointed out. So an objection was raised concerning the grandfather: if he has minor nephews in his household due to the father's death or poverty, it is not obligatory on him in the apparent transmission, yet the cause is realized and it is not obligatory. What is said to repel the objection is the negation of the cause because guardianship is incomplete due to its transfer to him from the father, so it is like the guardianship of an executor, but that is not sound, because the executor does not support from his own wealth unlike the grandfather. When he has no wealth, he is like the father. Al-Kamal said: There is no escape from the objection except by giving preference to the transmission of Hasan that it is upon the grandfather. So the causality is established as they mentioned, and he chose it in al-Ikhtiyar and acted upon it in al-Durr.
Source pages p. 723

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) of the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. It opens with an etymology of 'Fitr' and 'Fitrah', then explains the legal issue. The author, Al-Tahtawi, comments on the matn's statement: 'It is obligatory upon a free Muslim...' The proof is the hadith reported by Abu Dawud. The hadith commands payment, and in Hanafi usul, amr (command) indicates wujub (obligation) although the hadith is ahad, so the level is wajib (not fard). A key point is the time of obligation: according to the school it is broadly (mawsu'an) throughout one's life before Eid, not fixed on the day of Eid personally. However, a minority view says it is specific to Eid day. The commentator prefers the latter. The conditions of obligation are: freedom, Islam, possession of nisab (owner of a minimum wealth that is surplus to basic needs and free from debt), and the time is dawn of Eid. The nisab for zakat al-fitr is distinct from that of zakat al-mal and is defined in three categories: (1) nisab requiring growth (for zakat), (2) nisab for four rulings (including fitr), (3) nisab for prohibition of begging. The text also discusses who pays for minors: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the guardian pays from the child's own wealth if the child is wealthy; Muhammad says it is not obligatory on the wealthy minor. The relied-upon view is that the wealthy minor's fitrah is paid from his wealth. The issue of the grandfather is discussed: in the apparent transmission, grandfather is not obligated to pay for grandchildren in his care if the father is dead or poor, because his guardianship is incomplete. However, the chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that the grandfather is like the father, based on the transmission of Hasan ibn Ziyad, and this is what is acted upon in later fatwa collections like Al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): The obligatory charity paid by Muslims at the end of Ramadan, before the Eid prayer, for self and dependents.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers a legal obligation. Here three types are distinguished.
ولاية مطلقة (wilayah mutlaqah): Absolute guardianship over a person and their wealth, which is the cause for obligation of fitrah on the guardian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the level of obligation (hukm) of Sadaqat al-Fitr?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah Mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib on every free Muslim who possesses surplus wealth above basic needs and debts, payable before Eid prayer, with distinct rules for dependents and a debated time scope.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate

For Whom Zakat al-Fitr is Due: Dependents and Guardianship
Detailed rulings on who must be paid for

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which dependents the guardian is not obligated to pay fitrah for and identify the condition under which voluntary payment is valid by istihsan.

Core Idea
Zakat al-Fitr is owed for those under full guardianship; for others, the guardian may pay voluntarily and it is valid by custom.

This lesson examines the precise categories of dependents for whom zakat al-Fitr is not obligatory on the guardian, including the mukatab, adult son, wife, and certain slaves. It also clarifies the important Hanafi principle of istihsan which validates voluntary payment due to customary permission, and highlights the intra-madhhab dispute regarding jointly owned slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excluded dependents
List who the text explicitly excludes: mukatab, adult son, wife, jointly owned slave (according to Imam), misappropriated/captive slave.
Memorize these categories.
2
Understand the legal cause (sabab) of exclusion
Each exclusion is based on the guardian's lack of complete guardianship (wilayah) or ownership. The cause is absence of full authority.
This determines when the rule applies to analogous cases.
3
Analyse the istihsan exception
Despite no obligation, voluntary payment by the guardian is valid by istihsan due to customary permission; contrast with qiyas which would require invalidity.
Istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.
4
Examine the dispute on jointly owned slaves
Compare Imam's view (no obligation) with Sahibayn's (obligatory per head owned). Work through the nine-slave example to see the practical difference.
The thamarah al-khilaf is a real difference in distribution.
5
Apply the rule to misappropriated and captive slaves
Fitrah is not due during captivity, but becomes due upon return for the past period. Understand the timing of obligation.
This shows the ruling is conditional on possession.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (لا عن مكاتبه) لعدم الولاية، ولا تجب على المكاتب لأنّ ما في يده لمولاه .در قوله : (ولا ولده الكبير) أي الفقير، وإن كان في عياله لانعدام الولاية، ولو أدى عنه بغير إذنه فالقياس عدم الإجزاء كالزكاة، وفي الاستحسان الإجزاء لثبوت الأذن عادة ذكره العلامة نوح قوله: (وزوجته) لعدم الولاية الكاملة عليها، ولو أدى عنها بلا إذن جاز استحساناً للأذن عادة كالولد الكبير، وإن كان في عياله، وقيد به إشارة إلى أنه لو دفع عن الزوجة الناشزة والصغيرة التي لم تزف، وعن الابن الكبير الذي لم يكن في عياله لا يجوز عنهم إلا بالأمر كما يفيده القهستاني، وهل حكم الأجنبي إذا كان في عياله حكم الولد الكبير، ومقتضى ما في البحر عن الظهيرية الجواز كذا كتابة الدر. قوله : (وقن مشترك الخ لقصور الولاية والمؤنة في حق كل واحد منهما، وهذا عند الإمام، وقالا : تجب في العبيد المشتركة على كل من الشريكين فطرة ما يخصه من الرؤس دون الأشقاص نهر ، فلو كانت العبيد تسعة تجب عندهما في ثمانية فقط كذا في سكب الأنهر . قوله : (وكذا المغصوب المأسور) فلا تجب على سيدهما إلا بعد عودهما فتجب لما مضى كما في التنوير قوله : (أو زبيب جعل الزبيب كالتمر ،قولما وهو رواية عن الإمام وبها يفتي كما في البرهان والرواية الأخرى عن الإمام أنه كالبر. قوله : ( وهو ثمانية أرطال بالعراقي) والرطل العراقي مائة وثلاثون درهماً فالصاع ما يسع ألفاً، وأربعين درهماً، وقول أبي يوسف: الصاع ما خمسة أرطال وثلثا مراده بالرطل رطل المدينة، وهو ثلاثون أستار، أو رطل العراق يسع عشرون أستاراً، فيكون المجموع على القولين مائة وستين أستاراً والأستار ستة دراهم ونصف، وبعضهم جعل الخلاف حقيقياً، وما لم ينص عليه كذرة وخبز تعتبر فيه القيمة، وصدقة الفطر كالزكاة في المصارف ولا تجوز للذمي على المفتي به وهل يعتبر الصاع أو نصفه بالوزن، أو الكيل طريقتان ذكرهما الزيلعي . قوله : (ويجوز دفع القيمة قال في التنوير وجاز دفع القيمة في زكاة وعشر وخراج وفطرة ونذر وكفارة غير الاعتكاف ا هـ . قوله: (عند وجدان ما يحتاجه أي الفقير أي من هذه الأصناف التي تخرج منها الفطرة بأن كان الزمن زمن خصب. قوله : ( لقضاء حاجة الفقير) أي وحاجة الفقير متنوعة . قوله : ( وما يؤكل) أي ولو من غير هذه
His statement: (Not for his mukatab) due to lack of guardianship, and it is not obligatory upon the mukatab because what is in his hand belongs to his master. His statement: (Nor his adult son) meaning the poor one, even if in his household, due to absence of guardianship. If he pays on his behalf without his permission, the qiyas is non-validity like zakat, but by istihsan it is valid due to customary permission, as mentioned by Allamah Nuh. His statement: (And his wife) due to lack of complete guardianship over her. If he pays for her without permission, it is valid by istihsan due to customary permission like the adult son. However, if he pays for a rebellious wife or a minor wife not yet sent to him, or for an adult son not in his household, it is not valid except by order, as al-Qahastani indicates. The question of whether a stranger in his household is like the adult son: the implication of al-Bahr from al-Zahiriyya is permissibility. His statement: (And a jointly owned slave) due to deficiency of guardianship and maintenance in the right of each. This is according to Imam. The two said: it is obligatory in jointly owned slaves for each partner to pay the fitr of the heads that belong to him, not fractions. So if the slaves are nine, according to the two it is obligatory only for eight. His statement: (And similarly the misappropriated and captive) so it is not obligatory upon their master until they return, then it becomes obligatory for the past. His statement: (Or raisins) rendered raisins like dates, this is a transmission from Imam, and it is given fatwa upon as in al-Burhan. The other transmission from Imam is that it is like wheat. His statement: (And it is eight ratls by Iraqi measure) The Iraqi ratl is one hundred and thirty dirhams, so the sa' contains 1,040 dirhams. Abu Yusuf said: the sa' is five and two-thirds ratls, meaning by the ratl of Medina, which is thirty ustars, or the Iraqi ratl equals twenty ustars. So the total on both sayings is 160 ustars, and the ustar is six and a half dirhams. Some considered the difference real. For items not specified, like maize and bread, value is considered. Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat in disbursement and is not permissible for a dhimmī according to the muftā bihi. Whether the sa' or half is by weight or volume are two methods mentioned by al-Zayla'i. His statement: (And payment of value is permissible) He said in al-Tanwir: payment of value is permissible in zakat, 'ushr, kharaj, fitrah, nadhr, and kaffarah except i'tikaf. His statement: (When what he needs is found) meaning the poor person's need of these items from which fitrah is paid, when the time is one of abundance. His statement: (To meet the need of the poor) meaning the need of the poor is varied. His statement: (And what is eaten) meaning even if not from these
Source pages p. 724

Commentary
This passage continues the hashiah commentary on the matn, focusing on the precise list of dependents for whom the guardian must pay fitrah and the quantity. It begins with those for whom fitrah is not due: the mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) because the guardian lacks full ownership; the adult son, even if poor and living in his household, because guardianship is absent; similarly the wife, because guardianship is not complete. However, if the guardian pays on their behalf without explicit permission, it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) due to customary permission. The ruling is different for a rebellious wife or a minor wife not yet cohabited — payment without permission is not valid. For a jointly owned slave (qan mushtarak), Imam Abu Hanifa says fitrah is not obligatory because guardianship is deficient in both; but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is obligatory on each partner for the heads they own, not for fractions. The text then discusses the case of a misappropriated or captive slave: fitrah is not due until the slave returns, then it becomes due for the past period. Next, the quantity is discussed: the standard is half a sa' of wheat or its flour or saweeq (barley gruel), or a full sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. There is a difference within the Hanafi school: one transmission from Imam equates raisins with dates, another with wheat. The actual measure of the sa' is explained: eight ratls by Iraqi measure, which equals 1,040 dirhams, with another view from Abu Yusuf that the sa' is five and two-thirds ratls by Medinan measure, but both converge to 160 ustars (the ustar being 6.5 dirhams). The text also confirms that paying the cash value (qimah) is permissible and even preferable when the poor's need is best met by cash, though in times of hardship grain is better. Finally, it notes that fitrah is distributed like zakat to the eight categories, and it is not given to a dhimmi according to the muftā bihi.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract of manumission with his master, paying installments; his earnings are his own but ownership remains with the master.
قن مشترك (qan mushtarak): A slave jointly owned by two or more partners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man pays the fitrah of his adult son without the son's permission, what is the ruling?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated
B) It is valid by istihsan due to custom
C) It is valid only if the son is poor and in his house
D) It is valid only if the son is insane

Key Takeaway
Zakat al-Fitr is not obligatory on the guardian for certain dependents due to lack of full guardianship, but voluntary payment is valid by istihsan, and a key intra-madhhab dispute exists on jointly owned slaves.

Quantity and Types of Food in Zakat al-Fitr
Detailed rulings on the quantity and type of food

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the sa' for fitrah and identify the two transmissions regarding raisins, and apply the rule for paying value.

Core Idea
The prescribed quantity is half a sa' of wheat or a full sa' of dates/barley, but the value may be given when it better suits the poor's need.

This lesson details the specific quantities and types of food that can be given for zakat al-Fitr, focusing on the definition of the sa' in the Hanafi school, the dispute over whether raisins are measured like dates or wheat, and the important ruling that paying the cash value is permissible and even preferable in certain circumstances.

Guided Path
1
State the basic quantity for each food type
From the text: half a sa' of wheat, flour, or saweeq; full sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. Memorize the pairs.
This is the standard Hanafi rule.
2
Identify the dispute on raisins
One transmission from Imam equates raisins with dates (full sa'), another with wheat (half sa'). The mufta bihi is the first.
Know which transmission is relied upon for fatwa.
3
Define the sa' in Hanafi school
8 Iraqi ratls, equivalent to 1,040 dirhams, about 3.984 kg. Note Abu Yusuf's alternative definition and their convergence.
This is the volumetric measure; weight is approximate.
4
Evaluate the ruling on paying value (qimah)
Paying cash value is permissible, and in times of abundance it may be better to meet the poor's diverse needs.
This is a key practical ruling.
5
Understand disbursement rules
Fitrah is distributed like zakat (eight categories), not given to a dhimmi according to mufta bihi.
Disbursement mirrors zakat.

قوله: (لا عن مكاتبه) لعدم الولاية، ولا تجب على المكاتب لأنّ ما في يده لمولاه .در قوله : (ولا ولده الكبير) أي الفقير، وإن كان في عياله لانعدام الولاية، ولو أدى عنه بغير إذنه فالقياس عدم الإجزاء كالزكاة، وفي الاستحسان الإجزاء لثبوت الأذن عادة ذكره العلامة نوح قوله: (وزوجته) لعدم الولاية الكاملة عليها، ولو أدى عنها بلا إذن جاز استحساناً للأذن عادة كالولد الكبير، وإن كان في عياله، وقيد به إشارة إلى أنه لو دفع عن الزوجة الناشزة والصغيرة التي لم تزف، وعن الابن الكبير الذي لم يكن في عياله لا يجوز عنهم إلا بالأمر كما يفيده القهستاني، وهل حكم الأجنبي إذا كان في عياله حكم الولد الكبير، ومقتضى ما في البحر عن الظهيرية الجواز كذا كتابة الدر. قوله : (وقن مشترك الخ لقصور الولاية والمؤنة في حق كل واحد منهما، وهذا عند الإمام، وقالا : تجب في العبيد المشتركة على كل من الشريكين فطرة ما يخصه من الرؤس دون الأشقاص نهر ، فلو كانت العبيد تسعة تجب عندهما في ثمانية فقط كذا في سكب الأنهر . قوله : (وكذا المغصوب المأسور) فلا تجب على سيدهما إلا بعد عودهما فتجب لما مضى كما في التنوير قوله : (أو زبيب جعل الزبيب كالتمر ،قولما وهو رواية عن الإمام وبها يفتي كما في البرهان والرواية الأخرى عن الإمام أنه كالبر. قوله : ( وهو ثمانية أرطال بالعراقي) والرطل العراقي مائة وثلاثون درهماً فالصاع ما يسع ألفاً، وأربعين درهماً، وقول أبي يوسف: الصاع ما خمسة أرطال وثلثا مراده بالرطل رطل المدينة، وهو ثلاثون أستار، أو رطل العراق يسع عشرون أستاراً، فيكون المجموع على القولين مائة وستين أستاراً والأستار ستة دراهم ونصف، وبعضهم جعل الخلاف حقيقياً، وما لم ينص عليه كذرة وخبز تعتبر فيه القيمة، وصدقة الفطر كالزكاة في المصارف ولا تجوز للذمي على المفتي به وهل يعتبر الصاع أو نصفه بالوزن، أو الكيل طريقتان ذكرهما الزيلعي . قوله : (ويجوز دفع القيمة قال في التنوير وجاز دفع القيمة في زكاة وعشر وخراج وفطرة ونذر وكفارة غير الاعتكاف ا هـ . قوله: (عند وجدان ما يحتاجه أي الفقير أي من هذه الأصناف التي تخرج منها الفطرة بأن كان الزمن زمن خصب. قوله : ( لقضاء حاجة الفقير) أي وحاجة الفقير متنوعة . قوله : ( وما يؤكل) أي ولو من غير هذه
His statement: (Not for his mukatab) due to lack of guardianship, and it is not obligatory upon the mukatab because what is in his hand belongs to his master. His statement: (Nor his adult son) meaning the poor one, even if in his household, due to absence of guardianship. If he pays on his behalf without his permission, the qiyas is non-validity like zakat, but by istihsan it is valid due to customary permission, as mentioned by Allamah Nuh. His statement: (And his wife) due to lack of complete guardianship over her. If he pays for her without permission, it is valid by istihsan due to customary permission like the adult son. However, if he pays for a rebellious wife or a minor wife not yet sent to him, or for an adult son not in his household, it is not valid except by order, as al-Qahastani indicates. The question of whether a stranger in his household is like the adult son: the implication of al-Bahr from al-Zahiriyya is permissibility. His statement: (And a jointly owned slave) due to deficiency of guardianship and maintenance in the right of each. This is according to Imam. The two said: it is obligatory in jointly owned slaves for each partner to pay the fitr of the heads that belong to him, not fractions. So if the slaves are nine, according to the two it is obligatory only for eight. His statement: (And similarly the misappropriated and captive) so it is not obligatory upon their master until they return, then it becomes obligatory for the past. His statement: (Or raisins) rendered raisins like dates, this is a transmission from Imam, and it is given fatwa upon as in al-Burhan. The other transmission from Imam is that it is like wheat. His statement: (And it is eight ratls by Iraqi measure) The Iraqi ratl is one hundred and thirty dirhams, so the sa' contains 1,040 dirhams. Abu Yusuf said: the sa' is five and two-thirds ratls, meaning by the ratl of Medina, which is thirty ustars, or the Iraqi ratl equals twenty ustars. So the total on both sayings is 160 ustars, and the ustar is six and a half dirhams. Some considered the difference real. For items not specified, like maize and bread, value is considered. Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat in disbursement and is not permissible for a dhimmī according to the muftā bihi. Whether the sa' or half is by weight or volume are two methods mentioned by al-Zayla'i. His statement: (And payment of value is permissible) He said in al-Tanwir: payment of value is permissible in zakat, 'ushr, kharaj, fitrah, nadhr, and kaffarah except i'tikaf. His statement: (When what he needs is found) meaning the poor person's need of these items from which fitrah is paid, when the time is one of abundance. His statement: (To meet the need of the poor) meaning the need of the poor is varied. His statement: (And what is eaten) meaning even if not from these
Source pages p. 724

Commentary
This passage continues the hashiah commentary on the matn, focusing on the precise list of dependents for whom the guardian must pay fitrah and the quantity. It begins with those for whom fitrah is not due: the mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) because the guardian lacks full ownership; the adult son, even if poor and living in his household, because guardianship is absent; similarly the wife, because guardianship is not complete. However, if the guardian pays on their behalf without explicit permission, it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) due to customary permission. The ruling is different for a rebellious wife or a minor wife not yet cohabited — payment without permission is not valid. For a jointly owned slave (qan mushtarak), Imam Abu Hanifa says fitrah is not obligatory because guardianship is deficient in both; but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is obligatory on each partner for the heads they own, not for fractions. The text then discusses the case of a misappropriated or captive slave: fitrah is not due until the slave returns, then it becomes due for the past period. Next, the quantity is discussed: the standard is half a sa' of wheat or its flour or saweeq (barley gruel), or a full sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. There is a difference within the Hanafi school: one transmission from Imam equates raisins with dates, another with wheat. The actual measure of the sa' is explained: eight ratls by Iraqi measure, which equals 1,040 dirhams, with another view from Abu Yusuf that the sa' is five and two-thirds ratls by Medinan measure, but both converge to 160 ustars (the ustar being 6.5 dirhams). The text also confirms that paying the cash value (qimah) is permissible and even preferable when the poor's need is best met by cash, though in times of hardship grain is better. Finally, it notes that fitrah is distributed like zakat to the eight categories, and it is not given to a dhimmi according to the muftā bihi.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume; in the Hanafi school for zakat al-fitr it is defined as 8 Iraqi ratls, which is approximately 3.984 kg.
رطل عراقي (ratl iraqi): An Iraqi ratl equals 130 dirhams (approx. 409.5 g).
أستار (ustar): A unit of weight; 1 ustar = 6.5 dirhams (approx. 20.28 g).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Half a sa'
B) Full sa'
C) One mudd
D) Value equivalent to half a sa' of wheat

Key Takeaway
Fitrah is half a sa' of wheat or full sa' of other staples, with raisins following the full sa' mufta bihi, and paying cash value is permissible when it meets the poor's need.

Obligation and Amount of Sadaqat al-Fitr
Rulings on obligation, amount, time, and value payment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules of obligation, the required amount and types of food, the time of payment, and the permissibility of paying value in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib on every free Muslim who has surplus wealth, payable in food or value, with half a sa' of wheat or a full sa' of other staples.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah presents the core rulings on Sadaqat al-Fitr: who must pay, for whom, what to pay, and when. It also addresses the validity of paying cash instead of food and the importance of intention. Understanding these details ensures the obligation is fulfilled correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligee and the subjects of obligation
List the persons for whom a Muslim must pay fitrah (servants, mudabbar, umm walad) and those for whom it is not required (mukatib, adult son, wife, shared slave, runaway slave). Note the exceptions for non-Muslim servants.
The mukatib is considered a free person for fitrah purposes.
2
Determine the amount and qualifying items
The fitrah is half a sa' of wheat (or its flour or sawiq) or a full sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. Memorize the sa' as 8 Iraqi ratls (approx. 2.04 kg for wheat).
The choice of item affects the quantity.
3
Understand the time of obligation and recommended timing
The obligation begins at dawn of Eid al-Fitr. Paying before or after is valid but delaying is disliked. The best time is before going to the Eid musalla.
Early payment even before Ramadan is valid according to the authentic view.
4
Grasp the ruling on paying value
Paying the cash value of the required food is permitted and considered superior when the poor person's need is more quickly met. However, in times of hardship, giving actual food is better.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position; other schools forbid value payment.
5
Learn the intention requirement
Intention (niyyah) is required at the time of payment; it is sufficient if made when setting aside the amount, as in zakat.
Intention distinguishes fitrah from ordinary charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة
للخدمة، ومدبره وأم ولده ولو كفارا لا عن مكاتبه ولا ولده الكبير وزوجته، وقن مشترك وابق إلا بعد عوده، وكذا المغصوب والمأسور ، وهي نصف صاع من برأ ودقيقه أو سويقه، أو صاع تمر أو زبيب أو شعير وهو ثمانية أرطال بالعراقي ويجوز دفع القيمة، وهي أفضل عند وجدان ما يحتاجه لأنها أسرع لقضاء حاجة الفقير وإن كان زمن شدة فالحنطة، والشعير، وما يؤكل أفضل من الدراهم ووقت الوجوب عند طلوع فجر يوم الفطر فمن مات، أو افتقر قبله أو أسلم، أو اغتنى أو ولد بعده لا تلزمه ويستحب إخراجها قبل الخروج إلى المصلى، وصح لو قدم أو أخر والتأخير مكروه ويدفع كل شخص فطرته لفقير واحد، واختلف في جواز تفريق فطرة واحدة على أكثر من فقير، ويجوز دفع ما على جماعة لواحد على الصحيح والله الموفق للصواب.
هو
المذهب
الأعيان بأن يدفع عنها بالقيمة . قوله : (قبل الخروج إلى المصلى) بعد طلوع فجر الفطر عملاً بأمره وفعله در قوله وصح لو قدم أي ولو قبل رمضان على ما عليه عامة المتون، والشروح، وصححه غير واحد ورجحه في النهر، ونقل عن الولوالجية أنه ظاهر الرواية فكان در . قوله: (أو أخر) فوقتها موسع لا يضيق إلا في آخر العمر، وهو قول أصحابنا قالت العامة بدائع قوله : واختلف في جواز تفريق فطرة واحدة على أكثر من فقير) وعلى الجواز الأكثر وبه جزم في الولوالجية والخانية والبدائع والمحيط وتبعهم الزيلعي في الظهار من غير ذكر خلاف، وصححه في البرهان فكان هو المذهب، والأمر في حيث أغنوهم للندب فيفيد الأولوية در.
وبه
فرع من سقط عنه الصوم بعذر لم تسقط فطرته وقالوا في إخراجها قبول الصوم، والنجاح والفلاح والنجاة من سكرات الموت وعذاب القبر والنية فيها عند الدفع، ويكفي وجودها عند العزل على الظاهر كما في الزكاة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Kitab al-Zakat. For the servant, and his mudabbar and umm walad even if they are disbelievers, not for his mukatib, nor his adult son and his wife, and a shared slave and a runaway slave except after his return, and similarly the usurped and the captive. And it is half a sa' of wheat or its flour or its sawiq, or a sa' of dates or raisins or barley, and it is eight ratls by the Iraqi ratl. And payment of value is permitted, and it is superior when what he needs is found because it is quicker to fulfill the need of the poor. And if it is a time of hardship, then wheat, barley, and what is eaten are superior to dirhams. The time of obligation is at the dawn of the day of Fitr. So whoever dies, or becomes poor before it, or becomes Muslim, or becomes rich, or is born after it, it is not obligatory for him. And it is recommended to pay it before going out to the musalla. And it is valid if he pays early or late, and delaying is disliked. And each person pays his fitrah to one poor person. And there is disagreement on the permissibility of dividing one fitrah among more than one poor person. And paying the amount of a group to one person is permissible according to the correct view. And Allah is the granter of success to what is correct. That is the madhhab. The specific items by paying value for them. His saying: (before going out to the musalla) after dawn of the day of Fitr, acting upon his command and action. His saying: and it is valid if he pays early, even before Ramadan according to what is in most texts and commentaries, and more than one scholar authenticated it, and it was preponderated in al-Nahr, and it was transmitted from al-Walwalijiyyah that it is the apparent riwayah. His saying: (or delays) then its time is broad, it only narrows at the end of life, and it is the saying of our companions, the public scholars said in Bada'i'. His saying: and there is disagreement on the permissibility of dividing one fitrah among more than one poor person. And on permissibility is the majority, and it was decided in al-Walwalijiyyah, al-Khaniyyah, al-Bada'i', al-Muhit, and al-Zayla'i followed them in al-Zihar without mentioning any disagreement, and it was authenticated in al-Burhan, so it is the madhhab. And the command regarding when they have made them self-sufficient is for recommendation, giving priority. A branch: Whoever is excused from fasting, his fitrah is not dropped. And they said regarding its payment: acceptance of fasting, and success, and prosperity, and deliverance from the agonies of death and the punishment of the grave. And intention is required at the time of payment, and its existence at the time of setting aside is sufficient as apparent, as in zakat. And Allah most high knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the great.
Source pages p. 724

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah elaborates on the rules of Sadaqat al-Fitr (Zakat al-Fitr). It opens by listing for whom the obligation applies and for whom it does not: one must pay for one's servant, mudabbar, and umm walad even if they are non-Muslims, but not for a mukatib (slave contractually purchasing freedom), nor for an adult son living in his household (if poor), nor for his wife. For a shared slave (owned by multiple people) or an absconding slave, no fitrah is due from the master until the slave returns. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa; his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said that for jointly-owned slaves, each partner must pay fitrah for the number of heads proportionate to his share, disregarding fractional parts. The text then specifies the amount: half a sa' of wheat (or its flour or sawiq) or a full sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. A sa' is defined as eight Iraqi ratls. It permits paying the value (price) instead of the food item, and states that paying value is superior when the food items are available, as it is quicker to satisfy the poor person's need. However, in times of hardship, giving actual food (wheat, barley) is better than giving money. The time of obligation is at dawn of Eid al-Fitr. If someone dies, becomes poor, accepts Islam, becomes rich, or a child is born after this time, the fitrah is not obligatory. It is recommended to give it before leaving for the Eid prayer. Paying early (even before Ramadan) is valid, and delaying is disliked. The text then addresses distribution: each person should give his fitrah to a single poor person, but there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about dividing one fitrah among multiple poor persons. The majority (and the relied-upon view) permits it. Giving the fitrah of a group to one person is also permissible. Finally, a branch ruling: if a person is excused from fasting (e.g., due to travel or illness), his fitrah is not dropped; the obligation remains. The intention for fitrah is required at payment, and it suffices if the money is set aside with intention.

Key Terms
فطرة (fitrah): Sadaqat al-Fitr, the obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan before Eid prayer.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume equal to 8 Iraqi ratls, approximately 2.04 kg for wheat, 2.4 kg for barley/dates/raisins.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to override qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is correct about the time of obligation for Sadaqat al-Fitr?
A) It becomes wajib at sunset on the last day of Ramadan.
B) It becomes wajib at dawn of Eid al-Fitr.
C) It becomes wajib after the Eid prayer.
D) It is recommended to pay after the Eid prayer.

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr is a wajib charity with specific rules on amount, timing, and recipients; knowing these ensures valid fulfillment.

Disputes in Sadaqat al-Fitr: Shared Slave and Dividing Fitrah
Intra-Hanafi disputes on shared slave and dividing fitrah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two intra-Hanafi disputes mentioned in the Hashiyah: the obligation for a co-owned slave and the permissibility of dividing one fitrah among multiple poor persons.

Core Idea
Fatwa follows Sahibayn on shared slave and the majority on dividing fitrah among multiple poor.

This lesson zooms into two specific disagreements within the Hanafi school mentioned in al-Tahtawi's commentary. While the basic rulings are agreed, these two points have differing views between Imam Abu Hanifa and his students, and among later Hanafi scholars. Understanding these disputes sharpens your ability to identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the issue of the shared slave
The text says 'a shared slave' – a slave owned jointly by two or more persons. The question: does each co-owner have to pay fitrah for him?
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa says no fitrah is due from any co-owner because the ownership is incomplete. He analogizes to a runaway or usurped slave where the master does not pay.
Condition: complete ownership.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say each co-owner must pay fitrah in proportion to his share (ignoring fractions). They analogize to multiple heirs inheriting one slave.
Emphasis on benefit and partial ownership.
4
Identify the mufta bihi for shared slave
The fatwa is according to the Sahibayn, because it is more precautionary and prevents neglect of the obligation.
Tarjih by later scholars.
5
Address the second dispute: dividing one fitrah among multiple poor
The text mentions a disagreement on whether a single fitrah can be divided among more than one poor person. The majority (including al-Walwalijiyyah, al-Khaniyyah, al-Bada'i', al-Muhit, al-Zayla'i) permit it, and al-Burhan authenticated this as the madhhab.
The text earlier says 'each person pays his fitrah to one poor person' – that is the preferred practice, not a requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة
للخدمة، ومدبره وأم ولده ولو كفارا لا عن مكاتبه ولا ولده الكبير وزوجته، وقن مشترك وابق إلا بعد عوده، وكذا المغصوب والمأسور ، وهي نصف صاع من برأ ودقيقه أو سويقه، أو صاع تمر أو زبيب أو شعير وهو ثمانية أرطال بالعراقي ويجوز دفع القيمة، وهي أفضل عند وجدان ما يحتاجه لأنها أسرع لقضاء حاجة الفقير وإن كان زمن شدة فالحنطة، والشعير، وما يؤكل أفضل من الدراهم ووقت الوجوب عند طلوع فجر يوم الفطر فمن مات، أو افتقر قبله أو أسلم، أو اغتنى أو ولد بعده لا تلزمه ويستحب إخراجها قبل الخروج إلى المصلى، وصح لو قدم أو أخر والتأخير مكروه ويدفع كل شخص فطرته لفقير واحد، واختلف في جواز تفريق فطرة واحدة على أكثر من فقير، ويجوز دفع ما على جماعة لواحد على الصحيح والله الموفق للصواب.
هو
المذهب
الأعيان بأن يدفع عنها بالقيمة . قوله : (قبل الخروج إلى المصلى) بعد طلوع فجر الفطر عملاً بأمره وفعله در قوله وصح لو قدم أي ولو قبل رمضان على ما عليه عامة المتون، والشروح، وصححه غير واحد ورجحه في النهر، ونقل عن الولوالجية أنه ظاهر الرواية فكان در . قوله: (أو أخر) فوقتها موسع لا يضيق إلا في آخر العمر، وهو قول أصحابنا قالت العامة بدائع قوله : واختلف في جواز تفريق فطرة واحدة على أكثر من فقير) وعلى الجواز الأكثر وبه جزم في الولوالجية والخانية والبدائع والمحيط وتبعهم الزيلعي في الظهار من غير ذكر خلاف، وصححه في البرهان فكان هو المذهب، والأمر في حيث أغنوهم للندب فيفيد الأولوية در.
وبه
فرع من سقط عنه الصوم بعذر لم تسقط فطرته وقالوا في إخراجها قبول الصوم، والنجاح والفلاح والنجاة من سكرات الموت وعذاب القبر والنية فيها عند الدفع، ويكفي وجودها عند العزل على الظاهر كما في الزكاة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Kitab al-Zakat. For the servant, and his mudabbar and umm walad even if they are disbelievers, not for his mukatib, nor his adult son and his wife, and a shared slave and a runaway slave except after his return, and similarly the usurped and the captive. And it is half a sa' of wheat or its flour or its sawiq, or a sa' of dates or raisins or barley, and it is eight ratls by the Iraqi ratl. And payment of value is permitted, and it is superior when what he needs is found because it is quicker to fulfill the need of the poor. And if it is a time of hardship, then wheat, barley, and what is eaten are superior to dirhams. The time of obligation is at the dawn of the day of Fitr. So whoever dies, or becomes poor before it, or becomes Muslim, or becomes rich, or is born after it, it is not obligatory for him. And it is recommended to pay it before going out to the musalla. And it is valid if he pays early or late, and delaying is disliked. And each person pays his fitrah to one poor person. And there is disagreement on the permissibility of dividing one fitrah among more than one poor person. And paying the amount of a group to one person is permissible according to the correct view. And Allah is the granter of success to what is correct. That is the madhhab. The specific items by paying value for them. His saying: (before going out to the musalla) after dawn of the day of Fitr, acting upon his command and action. His saying: and it is valid if he pays early, even before Ramadan according to what is in most texts and commentaries, and more than one scholar authenticated it, and it was preponderated in al-Nahr, and it was transmitted from al-Walwalijiyyah that it is the apparent riwayah. His saying: (or delays) then its time is broad, it only narrows at the end of life, and it is the saying of our companions, the public scholars said in Bada'i'. His saying: and there is disagreement on the permissibility of dividing one fitrah among more than one poor person. And on permissibility is the majority, and it was decided in al-Walwalijiyyah, al-Khaniyyah, al-Bada'i', al-Muhit, and al-Zayla'i followed them in al-Zihar without mentioning any disagreement, and it was authenticated in al-Burhan, so it is the madhhab. And the command regarding when they have made them self-sufficient is for recommendation, giving priority. A branch: Whoever is excused from fasting, his fitrah is not dropped. And they said regarding its payment: acceptance of fasting, and success, and prosperity, and deliverance from the agonies of death and the punishment of the grave. And intention is required at the time of payment, and its existence at the time of setting aside is sufficient as apparent, as in zakat. And Allah most high knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the great.
Source pages p. 724

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah elaborates on the rules of Sadaqat al-Fitr (Zakat al-Fitr). It opens by listing for whom the obligation applies and for whom it does not: one must pay for one's servant, mudabbar, and umm walad even if they are non-Muslims, but not for a mukatib (slave contractually purchasing freedom), nor for an adult son living in his household (if poor), nor for his wife. For a shared slave (owned by multiple people) or an absconding slave, no fitrah is due from the master until the slave returns. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa; his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said that for jointly-owned slaves, each partner must pay fitrah for the number of heads proportionate to his share, disregarding fractional parts. The text then specifies the amount: half a sa' of wheat (or its flour or sawiq) or a full sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. A sa' is defined as eight Iraqi ratls. It permits paying the value (price) instead of the food item, and states that paying value is superior when the food items are available, as it is quicker to satisfy the poor person's need. However, in times of hardship, giving actual food (wheat, barley) is better than giving money. The time of obligation is at dawn of Eid al-Fitr. If someone dies, becomes poor, accepts Islam, becomes rich, or a child is born after this time, the fitrah is not obligatory. It is recommended to give it before leaving for the Eid prayer. Paying early (even before Ramadan) is valid, and delaying is disliked. The text then addresses distribution: each person should give his fitrah to a single poor person, but there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about dividing one fitrah among multiple poor persons. The majority (and the relied-upon view) permits it. Giving the fitrah of a group to one person is also permissible. Finally, a branch ruling: if a person is excused from fasting (e.g., due to travel or illness), his fitrah is not dropped; the obligation remains. The intention for fitrah is required at payment, and it suffices if the money is set aside with intention.

Key Terms
قن مشترك (qan mushtarak): A slave owned jointly by two or more persons.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to override qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relied-upon ruling (mufta bihi) regarding dividing one Sadaqat al-Fitr among multiple poor persons?
A) It is not allowed; each fitrah must go to one poor person.
B) It is allowed, and this is the madhhab according to the majority.
C) It is allowed only if the recipients are relatives.
D) It is allowed only if the total amount is at least one sa'.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi for shared slave is per Sahibayn (proportional payment), and dividing one fitrah among multiple poor is permissible.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Rulings of Zakat al-Fitr: Timing and Distribution
Commentary on Zakat al-Fitr covering timing and permissibility of giving to multiple poor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the timing of Zakat al-Fitr and explain the permissibility of distributing it to multiple recipients and paying value.

Core Idea
Zakat al-Fitr is valid early or late; paying value and distributing to multiple poor is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Zakat al-Fitr is a wajib charity at the end of Ramadan. This lesson examines key rulings from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: when it becomes obligatory, the recommended and valid times for payment, and the disagreement about how many poor may receive one person's Fitr. We will also see why paying value (qima) is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Zakat al-Fitr is wajib upon every free Muslim who has surplus provision on the day of Eid. The passage clarifies that it is not obligatory if one dies or becomes poor before that day.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because its dalil is zanni al-thubut.
2
Examine the timing of payment
The recommended time is before the Eid prayer after dawn. However, paying early (even before Ramadan) is valid and not disliked; delaying after Eid is makruh tanzihan but still valid.
The text emphasizes that the time is expansive and only becomes narrow at the end of life.
3
Analyze the distribution rulings
Each person normally pays to a single poor person, but there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: the majority (including al-Walwalijiyya, al-Khaniyya, al-Bada'i) permit dividing one Fitr among multiple poor. This is the relied-upon view.
Paying the value (price) instead of grain is also the madhhab, following the principle of 'huwa al-madhab'.
4
Understand the role of intention (niyya)
Intention is required at the time of payment. If one sets aside the amount with intention, that suffices, similar to the rule in regular Zakat.
This is based on the apparent view (azhar) of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مات، أو افتقر قبله أو أسلم، أو اغتنى أو ولد بعده لا تلزمه ويستحب إخراجها قبل الخروج إلى المصلى، وصح لو قدم أو أخر والتأخير مكروه ويدفع كل شخص فطرته لفقير واحد، واختلف في جواز تفريق فطرة واحدة على أكثر من فقير، ويجوز دفع ما على جماعة لواحد على الصحيح والله الموفق للصواب. هو المذهب الأعيان بأن يدفع عنها بالقيمة . قوله : (قبل الخروج إلى المصلى) بعد طلوع فجر الفطر عملاً بأمره وفعله در قوله وصح لو قدم أي ولو قبل رمضان على ما عليه عامة المتون، والشروح، وصححه غير واحد ورجحه في النهر، ونقل عن الولوالجية أنه ظاهر الرواية فكان در . قوله: (أو أخر) فوقتها موسع لا يضيق إلا في آخر العمر، وهو قول أصحابنا قالت العامة بدائع قوله : واختلف في جواز تفريق فطرة واحدة على أكثر من فقير) وعلى الجواز الأكثر وبه جزم في الولوالجية والخانية والبدائع والمحيط وتبعهم الزيلعي في الظهار من غير ذكر خلاف، وصححه في البرهان فكان هو المذهب، والأمر في حيث أغنوهم للندب فيفيد الأولوية در. وبه فرع من سقط عنه الصوم بعذر لم تسقط فطرته وقالوا في إخراجها قبول الصوم، والنجاح والفلاح والنجاة من سكرات الموت وعذاب القبر والنية فيها عند الدفع، ويكفي وجودها عند العزل على الظاهر كما في الزكاة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
If he dies, or becomes poor before it (Eid), or becomes Muslim, or becomes wealthy, or a child is born after it, it is not obligatory upon him. It is recommended to pay it before going out to the prayer place. It is valid if he pays early or delays, but delaying is disliked. Each person pays his Fitr to a single poor person. There is disagreement on the permissibility of dividing one Fitr among more than one poor person. It is permissible to pay what is due from a group to a single person according to the correct view. And Allah is the Guide to correctness. It is the relied-upon school to pay value in exchange for it. His saying: (before going out to the prayer place) after dawn of the day of Fitr, acting upon his command and action. His saying: and it is valid if he pays early, i.e., even before Ramadan according to the general texts and commentaries, and more than one scholar corrected it, and it was preferred in al-Nahr, and it was narrated from al-Walwalijiyya that it is the apparent transmission. His saying: (or delays) its time is expansive, not becoming narrow except at the end of life, and this is the saying of our companions. The general scholars said in Bada'i: his saying: (and there is disagreement on the permissibility of dividing one Fitr among more than one poor person) and the majority are upon permissibility, and it was affirmed in al-Walwalijiyya, al-Khaniyya, al-Bada'i, al-Muhit, and al-Zayla'i followed them in al-Zahir without mentioning disagreement, and it was corrected in al-Burhan, so it is the relied-upon school. The command where they enrich them is for recommendation, so it indicates preference. And by it a branch: the one for whom fasting is excused, his Fitr is not dropped. They said about paying it: acceptance of fasting, success, salvation from the throes of death and the punishment of the grave. Intention is required at the time of payment, and its presence at the time of setting aside suffices according to the apparent view, as in Zakat. And Allah Almighty knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 725

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi provides a detailed commentary on rulings of Zakat al-Fitr. It clarifies that Zakat al-Fitr is not obligatory upon a person who dies, becomes poor, or embraces Islam after the time of obligation. The recommended time is before the Eid prayer, and it can be paid well in advance (even before Ramadan) without being disliked. Delaying beyond Eid is makruh tanzihan. The text discusses disagreement about distributing one person's Fitr to multiple poor: the relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is permissible (jawaz), and this is affirmed by major Hanafi works. Paying the value (qima) is the madhhab. The passage also notes that intention (niyya) at the time of payment is required, but if one sets aside the amount, intention is sufficient. A person excused from fasting still owes Fitr. The commentary explains the reasoning behind these rulings.

Key Terms
فطرة (fitra): Zakat al-Fitr, or the charity given at the end of Ramadan.
نية (niyya): Intention required when paying Zakat al-Fitr; can be made when setting aside the amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on paying Zakat al-Fitr before Ramadan?
A) It is invalid
B) It is valid and recommended
C) It is valid but disliked
D) It is not allowed

Key Takeaway
Zakat al-Fitr is wajib; it can be paid early or late, and the relied-upon Hanafi position allows paying value and distributing to multiple poor.
